No One May Be Prevented from Using the Mosque
Ruling that no one can claim exclusive right to a mosque space

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that no one has exclusive right to any part of a mosque, cite the Quranic evidence, and apply the ruling to real scenarios.

Core Idea
No one owns a mosque; preventing anyone from worship is a major sin.

Mosques are for all believers. Yet some individuals, especially teachers, sometimes claim exclusive rights to certain spots or prevent others from using the mosque. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on this issue, supported by Quranic text and authoritative fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognise that the act in question is preventing a believer from worshipping or teaching in a mosque or claiming exclusive rights to a spot.
The ruling is that such prevention is prohibited (haram) and could be a major sin.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is Quran 72:18 ('And the mosques are for Allah'), which establishes that mosques belong solely to Allah and no human can claim ownership or exclusive use.
Also cited are fatwas from Imam al-Zahidi to support the ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse indicates exclusive ownership of Allah, negating any human right to monopolise a mosque space. If the mosque is for Allah, then all believers have equal access.
This is a clear and direct textual indication.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Awza‘i held that a regular occupant could evict a predecessor, but the Hanafi school (via al-Zahidi) rejects this.
The Hanafi position is consistent with the general principle that mosques are not owned by individuals.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi opinion is that no one has the right to evict another from a mosque space, as held by the later Hanafi authorities.
This ruling is relied upon in fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مدرستي، بسبب أوقات الصلاة أو لا فلا أو في بعضها ففي بعضها. كذا في فتح القدير. وفي العناية : والتدبير في الغلق لأهل المحلة فإنهم إذا اجتمعوا على رجل وجعلوه متولياً بغير أمر القاضي يكون متوليا ا هـ. وفي النهاية وكان المتقدمون يكرهون شد المصاحف واتخاذ المشدة لها كيلا يكون ذلك في صورة المنع من قراءة القرآن، فهذا مثله أو فوقه لأن المصحف ملك لصاحبه والمسجد ليس بملك لأحد ا.هـ. ومن هنا يعلم جهل بعض مدرسي زماننا من منعهم من يدرس في مسجد تقرر في تدريسه أو كراهتهم لذلك زاعمين الاختصاص بها دون غيرهم حتى سمعت من بعضهم أنه يضيفها إلى نفسه ويقول هذه مدرستي أو لا تدرس في وأعجب من ذلك أنه إذا غضب على شخص يمنعه من دخول المسجد خصوصاً أمر دنيوي وهذا كله جهل عظيم ولا يبعد أن يكون كبيرة فقد قال الله تعالى وإن المساجد الله ﴾ [الجن: ۱۸] وما تلوناه من الآية السابقة فلا يجوز لأحد مطلقاً أن يمنع مؤمناً من عبادة يأتي بها في المسجد لأن المسجد ما إلا لها من صلاة واعتكاف وذكر شرعي وتعليم علم وتعلمه وقراءة قرآن ولا يتعين مكان مخصوص لأحد حتى لو كان للمدرس موضع من المسجد يدرس فيه فسبقه غيره إليه ليس له إزعاجه وإقامته منه فقد قال الإمام الزاهدي في فتاويه المسماة بالقنية معزياً إلى فتاوي العصر له في المسجد موضع معين يواظب عليه وقد شغله غيره قال الأوزاعي له أن يزعجه وليس له ذلك عندنا ا هـ. ومن الفروع الدالة على أن مدرس المسجد كغيره ما قاله في القنية :أيضاً ليس للمدرس في المسجد أن يجعل من بيته باباً إلى المسجد وإن فعل أدى ضمان نقصان الجدار إن وقع فيه ا هـ. ذلك أن بعض مدرسي من أنه مدرسة وليس الأروام يعتقد في المسجد الذي له مدرس بمسجد حتى ينتهك حرمته بالمشي فيه بنعله المتنجس مع تصريح الواقف بجعله مسجداً، وسيأتي شروط المسجد إن شاء الله تعالى في كتاب الوقف.
My school, because of prayer times or not, or in some of them, so in some of them. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-‘Inayah: And the administration of the lock for the people of the neighborhood, for if they gather upon a man and make him a supervisor without the order of the judge, he is a supervisor. In al-Nihayah: The early scholars used to dislike tying the mus-hafs and making covers for them so that it would not be a form of preventing recitation of the Qur’an, so this is like that or worse because the mus-haf is the property of its owner while the mosque is not the property of anyone. Hence the ignorance of some teachers of our time is known, who prevent someone from teaching in a mosque assigned for his teaching or dislike that, claiming exclusive right to it over others, so that I heard from some of them that he adds it to himself and says 'this is my school' or 'do not teach in it'. And stranger than that is that when he becomes angry with a person he prevents him from entering the mosque, especially worldly matters. All of this is great ignorance and it is not far that it is a major sin. Allah said: 'And the mosques are for Allah' [al-Jinn 18] and what we have recited from the previous verse, so it is absolutely not permissible for anyone to prevent a believer from worship that he performs in the mosque, because the mosque is only for these things: prayer, i‘tikaf, lawful remembrance, teaching and learning knowledge, and reciting Qur’an. And no specific place is designated for anyone; even if a teacher has a specific spot in the mosque where he teaches and someone else precedes him to it, he does not have the right to disturb him and remove him from it. Imam al-Zahidi said in his fatwas called al-Qunyah, citing the fatwas of the era: 'If someone has a specific spot in the mosque that he regularly occupies, and someone else occupies it, al-Awza‘i said he may disturb him, but according to us he does not have that right.' Among the subsidiary issues indicating that the teacher in the mosque is like others is what he said in al-Qunyah: 'Also the teacher in the mosque cannot make a door from his house into the mosque, and if he does he is liable for compensation for the damage to the wall if any occurs.' That is because some teachers of the [probably Romans] believe about the mosque which has a teacher that it is his school and not a mosque, to the point of violating its sanctity by walking in it with his impure shoes, despite the endower explicitly making it a mosque. And the conditions of the mosque will come, Allah willing, in the book of waqf.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a ruling that no one has exclusive right to any part of a mosque. The author cites earlier scholars who disliked even tying mus-hafs to prevent their use, as this resembles monopolization. He then condemns teachers who claim a mosque spot as 'my school' and prevent others, stating it is great ignorance and possibly a major sin, citing Quran 72:18. He supports this with a fatwa from Imam al-Zahidi that a teacher cannot evict another who precedes him, and a subsidiary rule that a teacher cannot make a private door into the mosque. The ruling is that the mosque is for all believers; any action that excludes others is prohibited.

Key Terms
اختصاص (ikhtisas): Exclusive right or claim to a specific spot in the mosque
إزعاج (iz'aj): Disturbing or evicting someone from a place
القنية (al-qunyah): A collection of fatwas by Imam al-Zahidi

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the text, what is the ruling if a teacher has a specific spot in the mosque and someone else precedes him to it?
A) The teacher may evict the newcomer.
B) The teacher cannot evict him.
C) The teacher may wait until the newcomer leaves.
D) The mosques belongs to the teacher.

Key Takeaway
No one may be prevented from using a mosque for worship or learning; claiming exclusive rights is a major sin.

Sending Salawat in Every Du'a and Qunut
States the recommendation of salawat in every du'a and a rare variant ruling from al-Mujtaba.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended formula for salawat in du'a and qunut, and explain the ruling on the strange transmission from al-Mujtaba.

Core Idea
Sending salawat in every du'a, including qunut, is recommended; a rare report suggests it may replace salawat in tashahhud, but this is not the relied-upon view.

This lesson explores the recommendation of invoking blessings upon the Prophet in every supplication. The Hanafi school encourages salawat in all du'as, including the qunut of witr. However, a peculiar transmission in al-Mujtaba suggests a different approach, which this lesson will clarify.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its recommended ruling
The act is sending salawat in du'a and qunut. The passage states it is mustahabb (recommended).
2
Note the preferred formula
The recommended formula is 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad wa 'ala aali Muhammad'.
3
Examine the strange transmission from al-Mujtaba
This transmission states that if one says salawat in qunut, they do not say it in the final tashahhud; similarly for forgetfulness in the first sitting.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
This strange ruling is not the relied-upon view; the standard Hanafi position is to say salawat in both places.
5
Apply the principle of istihbab
Understand that recommendations (mandub) are not obligatory, so omitting salawat does not invalidate the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محجوب حتى يصلي على محمد وفي الواقعات : ويستحب في كل دعاء أن تكون فيه الصلاة على النبي اللهم صلي على محمد وعلى آل محمد اهـ . وهو يقتضي أنه يصلي عليه في القنوت بهذه الصيغة وهو الأولى. ومن الغريب ما في المجتبي : لو صلى على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في القنوت لا يصلي في القعدة الأخيرة، وكذا لو صلى عليه في القعدة الأولى سهواً لا يصلي عليه في القعدة الأخيرة ولا يصلي في القنوت اهـ . . رضي
Hidden until he prays upon Muhammad. In al-Waqi'at: It is recommended in every supplication that there be prayer upon the Prophet: 'O Allah, send prayers upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad' — end. This implies that one prays upon him in the qunut with this formula, and it is preferable. And among the strange things is what is in al-Mujtaba: If he prays upon the Prophet in the qunut, he does not pray (salawat) in the final sitting; similarly, if he prays upon him in the first sitting forgetfully, he does not pray upon him in the final sitting and does not pray (salawat) in the qunut — end.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. It discusses the recommendation of including salawat (prayer upon the Prophet) in every supplication, with the recommended formula being 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad wa 'ala aali Muhammad'. The author states that this implies it is recommended to say this in the qunut of witr. Then he mentions a strange transmission from al-Mujtaba: if one says salawat in the qunut, then he should not recite salawat in the final sitting (tashahhud); similarly, if he said it in the first sitting forgetfully, he does not recite it in the final sitting or in the qunut. This is a rare opinion and not the relied-upon position of the Hanafi school, which typically recommends salawat in both places.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): The supplication recited in the witr prayer.
الصلاة على النبي (al-salat 'ala al-nabi): The formula invoking blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad, e.g., 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the recommended action regarding salawat in qunut?
A) It is forbidden to say salawat in qunut.
B) It is recommended to say salawat in qunut with the formula 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad wa 'ala aali Muhammad'.
C) It is obligatory to say salawat in qunut.
D) Salawat in qunut cancels the need for salawat in the final sitting.

Key Takeaway
Sending salawat upon the Prophet in every du'a is a recommended act; the standard Hanafi position encourages it in both qunut and tashahhud independently.

Saying 'I am a Believer if Allah Wills': The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Dispute over istithna in iman and takfir implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on istithna' fi al-iman, distinguish it from the Shafi'i position, and state the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' is about future faith, not present doubt — the dispute hinges on intention.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a sensitive issue: the ruling on qualifying one's declaration of faith with 'if Allah wills'. While some scholars considered it kufr, the author clarifies the real disagreement revolves around whether one may link faith to Allah's will with the intention of iman al-muwafaat (faith at death). Understanding this distinction is crucial to avoid both theological error and unwarranted takfir.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and his companions: it is prohibited (makruh tahrimi or wajib to avoid) to say 'I am a believer if Allah wills' due to suspicion it creates, but it is not kufr.
The prohibition is precautionary.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
Al-Shafi'i and many early scholars permit it, citing Quran 18:23-24, because iman al-muwafaat is unknown and thus linking it to Allah's will is appropriate.
They argue it follows the Quranic command for future actions.
3
Follow the Hanafi response
Hanafi imams argue the Quranic verse applies to future acts, not present certain states. Attaching istithna' to a present declaration creates suspicion and may habituate the soul to doubt, leading to loss of faith.
The harm is spiritual corruption.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis must avoid the phrase; Shafi'is may use it. But the author strongly rejects the idea that it prevents marriage or justifies takfir.
The author condemns the extreme view of takfir as bigotry.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author affirms the majority Hanafi position of prohibition but clarifies that it is not kufr, citing Ibn al-Humam and quoting al-Subki's support for the permissive view among Salaf.
Mufta bihi: not kufr, but makruh tahrimi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تكفير من : موضع آخر مذبذبين بين ذلك لا إلى هؤلاء ولا إلى هؤلاء ﴾ [النساء : ١٤٣] فمن قال بالاستثناء في الإيمان فهو من جملة المذبذبين .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة والبزازية من كتاب النكاح عن الإمام أبي بكر محمد بن الفضل : من قال أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله فهو كافر لا تجوز المناكحة معه . قال الشيخ أبو حفص في فوائده : لا ينبغي للحنفي أن يزوج بنته من رجل شفعوي المذهب. وهكذا قال بعض مشايخنا ولكن يتزوج بنتهم . زاد في البزازية تنزيلاً لهم منزلة أهل الكتاب اهـ. وذهب طائفة إلى شك منهم في إيمانه بقوله «أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله على وجه الشك مطلقاً الحق لأنه وهو لا مسلم يشك في إيمانه . وقول الطائفة الأولى أنه يكفر غلط لأنه لا خلاف بين العلماء في أنه لا يقال أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله للشك في ثبوته للحال بل ثبوته في الحال مجزوم به كما نقله المحقق ابن الهمام في المسايرة، وإنما محل الاختلاف في جوازه لقصد إيمان الموافاة، فذهب أبو حنيفة وأصحابه إلى منعه وعليه الأكثرون، وأجازه كثير من العلماء منهم الشافعي وأصحابه لأن بقاءه إلى الوفاة عليه وهو المسمى بإيمان الموافاة غير معلوم، ولما كان ذلك هو المعتبر في النجاة كان هو الملحوظ عند المتكلم في ربطه بالمشيئة وهو أمر مستقبل، فالاستثناء فيه اتباع لقوله تعالى ولا تقولن لشيء إني فاعل ذلك غدا إلا أن يشاء الله ﴾ [الكهف : ۲۳] وقال أئمة الحنفية : لما كان ظاهر التركيب الإخبار بقيام الإيمان به في الحال مع اقتران كلمة الاستثناء به كان تركه أبعد عن التهمة فكان تركه واجباً، وأما من علم قصده فربما تعتاد النفس التردد لكثرة إشعارها بترددها في ثبوت الإيمان واستمراره وهذه مفسدة إذ قد يجر إلى وجوده آخر الحياة الاعتياد خصوصاً والشيطان منقطع مجرد نفسه لسبيل لا شغل له سواك فيجب ترك المؤدي إلى هذه المفسدة اهـ. فالحاصل أنه لا فائدة في هذا الشرط وهو قول الطائفة الثانية أن لا يكون شاكاً في إيمانه إذ لا مسلم يشك فيه، وأما التكفير بمطلق الاستثناء فقد علمت غلطه وأقبح من ذلك من منع منا كحتهم وليس هو إلا محض تعصب نعوذ بالله من شرور أنفسنا وسيئات أعمالنا، خصوصاً قد نقل الإمام السبكي في رسالة ألفها في هذه المسألة : أن القول بدخول الاستثناء في الإيمان هو : و قول أكثر السلف من الصحابة والتابعين ومن بعدهم والشافعية والمالكية والحنابلة ومن المتكلمين الأشعرية والكلابية قال : وهو قول سفيان الثورى اهـ. فالقول بتكفير هؤلاء من أقبح الأشياء.
Takfir of whoever: another place 'wavering between this and that, belonging neither to these nor to those' [Quran 4:143]. So whoever uses istithna' in iman is among the waverers. End. And in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya from the book of marriage from Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl: whoever says 'I am a believer if Allah wills' is a disbeliever, marriage with him is not permissible. Shaykh Abu Hafs said in his Fawa'id: it is not appropriate for a Hanafi to marry his daughter to a Shafi'i man. Similarly some of our shaykhs said, but they may marry their daughter. al-Bazzaziyya added: treating them like People of the Book. End. A group held that there is doubt in their iman by saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' in the sense of absolute doubt, but this is wrong because no Muslim doubts his iman. The first group's saying that he is a kafir is a mistake because there is no disagreement among scholars that one should not say 'I am a believer if Allah wills' out of doubt about its current existence; rather its current existence is certain, as transmitted by al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam in al-Musayara. The only point of disagreement is its permissibility when intending iman of the end (iman al-muwafaat). Abu Hanifa and his companions forbade it, and the majority agree, while many scholars including al-Shafi'i and his companions permitted it because survival until death with iman, called iman al-muwafaat, is unknown. Since that is what matters for salvation, it is what the speaker considers when linking it to the divine will, which is a future matter. So istithna' in it follows the verse 'And never say of anything, 'Indeed, I will do that tomorrow,' except [when adding], 'If Allah wills.'' [Quran 18:23-24]. Hanafi imams said: Since the apparent construction informs of the present existence of iman while the istithna' particle is attached, leaving it out is farther from suspicion, so leaving it is obligatory. As for one whose intention is known, the soul may become accustomed to hesitation due to its frequent suggestion of indecision about the existence and continuity of iman, and this is a corruption that may lead to loss of iman at the end of life, especially since Satan is devoted solely to this. So it is obligatory to avoid what leads to this corruption. End. The conclusion is that there is no benefit in this condition—the second group's saying that one should not doubt his iman, since no Muslim doubts it. As for declaring kufr due to absolute istithna', you have learned its error. Worse than that is preventing marriage with them; it is nothing but pure bigotry. We seek refuge in Allah from the evils of our souls and the evil of our deeds. Especially since Imam al-Subki transmitted in a treatise on this issue that the view permitting istithna' in iman is the view of most of the Salaf among the Sahaba and Tabi'un and those after them, and the Shafi'is, Malikis, Hanbalis, and among the theologians the Ash'aris and Kalabiyya. He said it is the view of Sufyan al-Thawri. End. So declaring these people as disbelievers is among the ugliest things.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling on saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' (al-istithna' fi al-iman). The author first presents a strict view from some Hanafis that such a statement constitutes kufr and prohibits marriage. He then critiques this view, distinguishing between doubt about present iman (which is impermissible and agreed upon) and the permissibility of linking one's iman to Allah's will with the intention of iman al-muwafaat (faith at the end of life). Abu Hanifa and the majority of Hanafis prohibit the statement to avoid suspicion and potential harm, while al-Shafi'i and many others permit it based on Quranic precedent. The author strongly rejects takfir of those who use istithna', citing the support of many scholars including al-Subki. The relied-upon position is that it is not kufr but rather makruh or permissible depending on intention.

Key Terms
إيمان الموافاة (iman al-muwafaat): Faith at the moment of death, which determines salvation.
الاستثناء في الإيمان (al-istithna' fi al-iman): Adding 'if Allah wills' when declaring one's faith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary point of disagreement between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding 'ana mu'min in sha'a Allah'?
A) Whether it is kufr or not
B) Whether it is permissible when intending iman al-muwafaat
C) Whether it is allowed in prayer
D) Whether it is a condition for marriage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' as a precaution, but it is not kufr; the disagreement with Shafi'is is about intention for future faith.

The Two Types of Vows and Their Core Conditions
Defining unconditional and conditional vows and their conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish unconditional (munjaz) from conditional (mu'allaq) vows and state the two core conditions for a valid vow in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Only an intrinsically intended worship of an obligatory type can be validly vowed.

Vows (nadhr) are serious commitments to Allah. The Hanafi school divides them into two categories: unconditional (munjaz) and conditional (mu'allaq). But not every good deed can be vowed – the text from al-Bada'i sets conditions that clarify which acts of devotion are eligible. This lesson will walk you through the classification and the key conditions so you can identify a valid vow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of vows
The passage opens by categorizing vows as unconditional (munjaz) or conditional (mu'allaq). An unconditional vow is an immediate obligation not tied to a future event. A conditional vow depends on a future occurrence (e.g., 'If Allah heals my son, I owe a fast').
The hadith prohibition is often applied to conditional vows that resemble compensation.
2
Extract the conditions for a valid unconditional vow
The text then lists what makes a vowed act binding: it must be (a) an act of worship intended in itself (ibadah maqsudah bi nafsiha) and (b) of a type that has an obligatory equivalent in the Shari'ah (min jinsiha wajib). Acts that are means to an end (e.g., wudu, adhan) or that are not obligatory in their kind (e.g., visiting the sick) do not qualify.
These conditions come from al-Bada'i and are the relied-upon (zahir al-riwayah) position.
3
Apply the conditions to examples
The passage provides many examples: vowing permissible acts (eating, drinking) is not binding; vowing acts that are not intrinsically intended (wudu for every prayer, sajdat al-tilawa according to the preferred view) is not binding; vowing acts without an obligatory equivalent (visiting the sick) is not binding. On the other hand, vowing prayer, fasting, or Hajj is binding because they meet both conditions.
For prayer, the minimum is two rak'ahs even if one says 'a prayer' or 'a day' of prayer.
4
Note the distinction between unconditional and conditional vows regarding the hadith
The passage ends by discussing the hadith that seems to discourage vows. It explains that the prohibition applies to conditional vows where the worshipper attaches the vow to a desired outcome, tainting it with the idea of compensation. An unconditional vow of devotion is purely for Allah and not prohibited.
This is an important usul point: a general prohibition can be narrowed by considering the 'illa (cause).

Source Text

ثم المنذور قسمان: منجز ومعلق . فالمنجز يلزم الوفاء به إن كان عبادة مقصودة بنفسها ومن جنسها واجب فيحرم عليه الوفاء بنذر معصية، ولا يلزمه بنذر مباح من أكل وشرب ولبس وجماع وطلاق ولا بنذر ما ليس بعبادة مقصودة كنذر الوضوء لكل صلاة، وكذا لو نذر سجدة التلاوة خلافاً لما في القنية من أنها تلزمه بخلاف ما إذا قال سجدة لا تلزمه، ولا بنذر ما ليس من جنسه واجب كعيادة المريض وتشييع الجنازة. قال في البدائع : ومن شروطه أن يكون قربة مقصودة فلا يصح النذر بعيادة المرضى وتشييع الجنائز والوضوء والاغتسال ودخول المسجد المصحف والأذان وبناء الرباطات والمساجد وغير ذلك وإن كانت قرباً ومس لأنها غير مقصودة. فلو قال لله علي أن أصلي أو أصلي صلاة أو علي صلاة لزمه ركعتان، وكذا لو قال لله علي أن أصلي يوماً لزمه ركعتان كما في القنية، فلو نذر صلوات شهر فعليه صلوات شهر كالمفروضات مع الوتر دون السنن لكنه يصلي الوتر والمغرب أربعاً. ولو نذر أن يصلي ركعة لزمه ركعتان أو ثلاثاً فأربع لأن ذكر بعض ما لا يتجزأ كذكر كله كما عرف. ولو نذر نصف ركعة لزمه ركعتان عند أبي يوسف وهو المختار كما في الخلاصة والتجنيس، ولو نذر أن يصلي الظهر ثمانياً أو أن يزكي النصاب عشراً أو حجة الإسلام مرتين لا يلزمه الزائد لأنه التزام غير المشروع فهو نذر بمعصية كما لو نذر صلاة بغير وضوء لأنها ليست بعبادة بخلاف ما لو نذرها بغير قراءة أو عرياناً فإنها تلزمه بقراءة مستوراً على المختار لأنها بغير قراءة عبادة كصلاة المأموم والأمي وبغير ثوب لعادمه والظاهر أن مرادهم بغير وضوء بغير طهارة أصلاً تجوزاً بالخاص عن العام ليكون المشروع الأصلي في مثله هو الخاص وإلا فالصلاة بغير وضوء مشروعة بالتيمم عند العجز عن استعمال الماء. وينبغي أن يلزم النذر بالصلاة بغير طهارة على قول أبي يوسف كما قال به بغير وضوء لأنه يقول بمشروعيتها لفاقد الطهورين كما عرف، وكأنه لنذرته لم يفرغ عليه. وفي شرح المجمع لمصنفه : لو قال صلاة بطهارة بلا طهارة يلزمه بطهارة اتفاقاً . موجب النذر لأن نفس النذر بالقربة قربة فيبطل بالردة كسائر القرب ا هـ . ففيه التصريح بأن النذر بالقربة قربة فليس بمنهي عنه فيتعين تأويل الحديث بالمعلق بما لا يريد كونه (كـ(إن) دخلت دار فلان كذا ونحوه فإنه لم يقصد به القربة وكذا المعلق بما يريد كونه (كـ(إن) شفى الله فلله علي صوم مريضي أو رد غائبي فلله علي كذا فإنه لم يخلص من شائبة العوض حيث جعل القربة في مقابلة ما فيه من إيهام أن الشفاء حصل بسببه فلذا قال في الحديث «إنه لا يرد شيئاً وإنما يستخرج به من «البخيل فإن هذا الكلام قد وقع موقع التعليل للنهي بخلاف النذر غير المعلق على شيء أصلاً فإنه تبرع محض بالقربة الله تعالى فلا وجه لجعله داخلاً تحت النهي. هذا وقد حمل بعض شراح البخاري النهي في الحديث على من يعتقد أن الندر مؤثر في تحصيل غرضة المعلق عليه وما قلناه أقرب والله تعالى أعلم قوله : (ومن جنسها (واجب) انظر ما فائدة التقييد به فإن عيادة المريض وتشييع الجنازة قد خرجنا بعبادة مقصودة كما يصرح به ما سينقله عن البدائع قوله : (وينبغي أن يلزم
Then the vowed act is of two types: unconditional (munjaz) and conditional (mu'allaq). The unconditional must be fulfilled if it is a worship intended in itself and of a type that is obligatory. So it is forbidden to fulfill a vow of disobedience, and he is not bound by a vow of permissible acts like eating, drinking, wearing, intercourse, and divorce, nor by a vow of something that is not an intended worship like vowing ablution for every prayer, and likewise if he vows a prostration of recitation contrary to what is in al-Qunya that it binds him, unlike if he says 'a prostration' it does not bind him. Nor is he bound by a vow of something not of a type that is obligatory, like visiting the sick and following a funeral. He said in al-Bada'i: Among its conditions is that it be an intended act of devotion, so vowing visiting the sick, following funerals, ablution, bathing, entering the mosque, touching the mushaf, adhan, building ribats and mosques, etc., is not valid even though they are acts of devotion and benefit, because they are not intended [in themselves]. So if he says 'I owe to Allah that I pray' or 'I pray a prayer' or 'upon me is a prayer', he is bound to pray two rak'ahs. Likewise if he says 'I owe to Allah that I pray for a day', he is bound to two rak'ahs as in al-Qunya. If he vows prayers of a month, he must perform prayers of a month like the obligatory ones with the witr but not the sunnah prayers; however he prays the witr and Maghrib as four. If he vows to pray one rak'ah, he is bound to two; if three, then four, because mentioning part of something indivisible is like mentioning the whole, as is known. If he vows half a rak'ah, he is bound to two rak'ahs according to Abu Yusuf, and that is the chosen view as in al-Khulasa and al-Tajnis. If he vows to pray Dhuhr eight rak'ahs, or to give zakat on a nisab ten times, or to perform Hajj al-Islam twice, the excess is not binding because it is an undertaking of what is not prescribed, so it is a vow of disobedience, like vowing prayer without wudu because it is not a worship. Contrary to vowing it without recitation or naked, then it is binding upon him to pray with recitation and covered according to the chosen view, because prayer without recitation is a worship like the prayer of a follower and an illiterate person, and without a garment for one who lacks it. And it appears that by 'without wudu' they mean without any purification at all, by metonymy of the specific for the general, so that the originally prescribed in such a case is the specific; otherwise prayer without wudu is prescribed with tayammum when unable to use water. It should be that the vow of prayer without purification is binding according to Abu Yusuf, as he said regarding without wudu, because he holds it prescribed for one lacking the two purifiers, as is known. And it is as if he did not complete the vow. In Sharh al-Majma' by its author: If one says 'prayer with purification without purification', it is binding with purification unanimously. The cause of the vow's obligation is that the vow itself of an act of devotion is an act of devotion, so it is invalidated by apostasy like other acts of devotion. So in that is an explicit statement that the vow of an act of devotion is an act of devotion, so it is not prohibited, so the hadith must be interpreted as referring to the conditional vow for something one does not want to happen (like 'if I enter such-and-such house, then I owe something'), and likewise the conditional vow for something one wants to happen (like 'if Allah heals so-and-so, I owe a fast') is not free from the taint of compensation, where he makes the devotion in exchange for an implication that healing occurred due to him. That is why the hadith says 'it does not avert anything' etc. This then is the explanation for the prohibition. He said: (and of its type obligatory) look what is the benefit of this restriction, then visiting the sick and funerals we have excluded by the condition of intended worship, as will be transmitted from al-Bada'i. He said: (and it should be binding...).
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed classification of vows and their conditions. Vows are divided into unconditional (munjaz) and conditional (mu'allaq). An unconditional vow must be fulfilled if it is an act of worship that is intrinsically intended (maqsudah bi nafsiha) and of a type that is obligatory in the Shari'ah. Vows of disobedience are forbidden to fulfill, and vows of permissible acts are not binding. The text lists several examples: vowing to perform wudu for every prayer, vowing a prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawa) – with a difference from al-Qunya – vowing acts that are not intrinsically intended (like visiting the sick, following funerals, etc.) are not valid. The conditions from al-Bada'i are reiterated: the vow must be for an act of devotion that is intended in itself. The text then discusses specific scenarios: if one vows to pray, the minimum is two rak'ahs; if one vows prayers for a month, it is like the obligatory prayers including witr but not sunnah; if one vows a single rak'ah, it becomes two; if half a rak'ah, it becomes two according to Abu Yusuf. Vowing an excess beyond the prescribed limits (e.g., eight rak'ahs for Dhuhr, double zakat, double Hajj) is not binding because it is an innovation and a vow of disobedience. The discussion then addresses vowing prayer without wudu or without purification, with differences among the Hanafi imams. Finally, the passage returns to the hadith interpretation: the prohibition is on conditional vows that have a taint of compensation, not on unconditional vows of devotion. The commentary from the author of al-Majma' is cited, emphasizing that the vow of an act of devotion is itself an act of devotion and not subject to the prohibition.

Key Terms
المنجز (al-munjaz): An unconditional vow, not tied to a condition.
المعلق (al-mu'allaq): A conditional vow, dependent on a future event.
عبادة مقصودة بنفسها (ibadah maqsudah bi nafsiha): A worship that is intended for its own sake, not as a means to another worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a valid subject of a vow?
A) Vowing to build a mosque.
B) Vowing to perform the Eid prayer.
C) Vowing to feed the poor every Friday.
D) Vowing to recite the Qur'an daily.

Key Takeaway
A vow only becomes binding if the vowed act is an intrinsically intended form of worship that has an obligatory counterpart in Islamic law.

intermediate
10 min
Intra-Hanafi Differences on Vowing Specific Acts
Specific applications and intra-Hanafi differences on vow rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi conditions to complex cases (e.g., vowing half a rak'ah, prayer without wudu) and identify the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Vowing an indivisible act obligates the minimum whole; vowing a non-worship with conditions may still be binding through correction.

The previous lesson established the general conditions for a valid vow. This lesson delves into the specific rulings that arise when the vow touches on unusual or borderline acts: vowing a fraction of a rak'ah, vowing prayer without purification, or vowing an excessive number of units. The Hanafi imams sometimes differ on these nuances, and the mufta bihi is determined by later authority. This lesson walks you through these scenarios so you can navigate the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Analyze vowing a specific number of rak'ahs
The passage provides clear rules: If one vows 'a prayer' or 'a day of prayer', two rak'ahs are obligatory (minimum). If one vows one rak'ah, it becomes two because a rak'ah is indivisible; mentioning part obligates the whole. For three rak'ahs, it becomes four. For half a rak'ah, it becomes two according to Abu Yusuf, which is the chosen view (al-mukhtar).
This is based on the principle that prayer units cannot be fractioned.
2
Understand vowing prayer without essential conditions
Vowing prayer without wudu (or without purification) is problematic. The passage distinguishes: vowing prayer without wudu is like vowing a sin and not binding according to the majority. However, Abu Yusuf holds it binding because he considers prayer with tayammum as valid for those unable to use water. The mufta bihi is that the vow binds the person to perform the prayer properly with wudu/tayammum.
Sharh al-Majma' states that a vow of 'prayer with purification without purification' is binding unanimously, interpreting 'without purification' as a slip.
3
Examine vowing excessive acts
If one vows to pray Dhuhr eight rak'ahs, to give zakat ten times, or to perform Hajj twice, the extra is not binding. These exceed the prescribed limits and are therefore considered vows of disobedience (like vowing a sin).
This shows the condition 'min jinsiha wajib' – only the obligatory pattern binds; innovation is not a valid vow.
4
Synthesize the hierarchy of authority
The passage cites al-Khulasa and al-Tajnis for preferring Abu Yusuf's view on half rak'ah. It also cites Sharh al-Majma' for unanimity on the purification issue. This demonstrates how later works (mutakhkhirin) settle the ikhtilaf.
The mufta bihi is the operative position for fatwa.

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed classification of vows and their conditions. Vows are divided into unconditional (munjaz) and conditional (mu'allaq). An unconditional vow must be fulfilled if it is an act of worship that is intrinsically intended (maqsudah bi nafsiha) and of a type that is obligatory in the Shari'ah. The text then discusses specific scenarios: if one vows to pray, the minimum is two rak'ahs; if one vows prayers for a month, it is like the obligatory prayers including witr but not sunnah; if one vows a single rak'ah, it becomes two; if half a rak'ah, it becomes two according to Abu Yusuf. Key Terms
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen view on which fatwa is based.
ما لا يتجزأ (ma la yatajazza'): That which is indivisible, e.g., a single rak'ah of prayer.
من جنسها واجب (min jinsiha wajib): Of a type that has an obligatory counterpart in the Shari'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if someone vows to pray Dhuhr eight rak'ahs, what is the ruling?
A) He must pray eight rak'ahs.
B) He must pray four rak'ahs (the prescribed number).
C) The vow is completely invalid and he owes nothing.
D) He must pray eight but split into two sets of four.

Key Takeaway
When a vow involves a fraction or an improper condition, the Hanafi school corrects it to the complete and proper act of worship.

Refining the Applicability of a Ruling: The Case of Sacrificing a Rooster
Critical refinement on the relevance of a Dhakhira quotation to the discussion of ta'rīf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate whether a quoted ruling applies to a new case by examining the presence or absence of the effective cause ('illa).

Core Idea
A ruling only transfers if its 'illa is present; if the 'illa is absent, the case stands apart.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Rā'iq examines a previous quotation from al-Dhakhīra about the karāhah of sacrificing a rooster. He argues that this example does not directly support the discussion of ta'rīf because the reason behind the karāhah—imitating Magians—is not present in the current context. Yet he leaves open the possibility that a broader common element might exist. This lesson teaches you how to critically assess the relevance of a precedent case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original case and ruling
The Dhakhīra states that sacrificing a rooster in imitation of Magians is makrūh (disliked). Note the ruling and its basis.
2
Identify the new case under discussion
The discussion is about the ruling on ta'rīf (standing at ‘Arafāt), specifically regarding imitating the pilgrims. This is the context where the Dhakhīra quotation was cited.
The author’s current discussion is about ta'rīf.
3
Extract the 'illa from the original case
The reason ('illa) for karāhah is that the act is from the customs of the Magians (min rusūm al-majūs). This is the specific effective cause.
4
Check if the 'illa is present in the new case
The author states that this 'illa is absent here (muntafiyah huna). Imitating pilgrims is not the same as imitating Magians.
The absence of the specific 'illa breaks the qiyās.
5
Consider the hypothetical common element
The author mentions that if one argues that the common element is mere resemblance (tashabbuh), the analogy might hold. But he leaves this as a possibility, not a confirmed ruling.
This step shows the subtlety in refining analogies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وفي الذخيرة من كتاب الخطر والإباحة الخ فيه أنه لا شاهد فيه لما نحن فيه لما أن العلة في كراهة التضحية كونها من رسوم المجوس وهي منتفية هنا إلا أن يقال : إن الجامع التشبه في كل
He said: (And in al-Dhakhira from the book of danger and permission etc.) In it there is no proof for what we are discussing because the reason for the karahah of the sacrifice is that it is from the customs of the Magians, and that is absent here, unless it is said that the common element is resemblance in everything.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on a previous quotation from al-Dhakhira. The Dhakhira had said that sacrificing a rooster or chicken in imitation of those who sacrifice is makruh because it is from the customs of the Magians. The author comments that this example does not apply to the current discussion (ta'rif) because the reason for karahah in the Dhakhira is that it imitates the Magians, which is not relevant to imitating the pilgrims at 'Arafat. However, he suggests a possible common element: the act of resemblance (tashabbuh) in both cases. The text is incomplete, but the point is to refine the applicability of the analogy.

Key Terms
الذخيرة (al-Dhakhīra): A Hanafi fiqh work by Burhān al-Dīn al-Marghīnānī (author of al-Hidāyah).
العلة (al-ʻilla): The effective cause or ratio legis that grounds a legal ruling; essential for qiyās.
التشبه (al-tashabbuh): Resemblance or imitation; the proposed common element between the two cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider the Dhakhīra quotation not applicable to the discussion of ta'rīf?
A) Because the Dhakhīra deals with sacrifices, not standing.
B) Because the reason for makrūh there is imitating Magians, not imitating pilgrims.
C) Because the Dhakhīra is not a reliable source.
D) Because ta'rīf is always permissible.

Key Takeaway
A ruling from one case cannot be transferred to another unless the effective cause ('illa) is present in the new case.

Can One Say That the Supplication of a Disbeliever Is Accepted?
Discusses the differing opinions on the permissibility of stating that the supplication of disbelievers may be answered.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the permissibility of saying that the supplication of a disbeliever may be accepted, and cite the Quranic evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
The disagreement is about legal, not rational, permissibility; Quranic evidence shows Allah answers even disbelievers in distress.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the commentator clarifies a nuanced point: is it legally permissible to state that the supplication of a disbeliever may be answered? Some had reduced the matter to mere rational possibility, but the author insists it is a question of shar‘i permissibility. He then provides Quranic proof (Surah al-‘Ankabut and Surah al-Hijr) to support the view that such a statement is allowed, and states that the fatwa is based on this.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
What exactly is being disputed? The disagreement is about the permissibility of saying that the supplication of a disbeliever may be accepted.
The author distinguishes between rational and legal permissibility.
2
Distinguish between rational and legal permissibility
Some scholars interpreted the permissibility as merely rational (i.e., it is possible in the mind). The author rejects this because the discussion is about what is legally allowed to be said.
Legal permissibility requires a textual basis (dalil).
3
Examine the evidence
The author cites two Quranic verses: 29:65 (disbelievers call upon Allah sincerely aboard ships) and 15:36 (Iblis's supplication for respite was answered). These show that Allah does answer the supplications of disbelievers in certain contexts.
The evidence supports the legal permissibility of stating that their supplication may be answered.
4
Note the conclusion
The author states that this is the basis of the fatwa (mufta bihi). The Hanafi position is that it is legally permissible to say that a disbeliever's supplication may be accepted.
This conclusion affects other rulings, such as allowing disbelievers to attend prayers for rain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : اختلفوا في أنه هل يجوز) قال في النهر : أي يجوز عقلاً وإن لم يقع ا ا هـ. وهو بعيد جداً ومما يبعده نسبة الجواز إلى القول لا إلى الاستجابة ولا معنى للاختلاف في جواز القول بها عقلاً، فالظاهر أن المراد الجواز شرعاً يدل عليه قوله في غرر الأذكار : ورأى مالك حضوره لأن دعاءه قد يستجاب في الشدة لقوله تعالى فإذا ركبوا في الفلك دعوا الله مخلصين له الدين [العنكبوت : ٦٥] الآية | هـ . قلت : ولقوله تعالى قال رب انظرني إلى يوم يبعثون قال إنك من المنظرين [ الحجر : ٣٦] ولعل هذا وجه ما عليه الفتوى .
His saying: 'They disagreed on whether it is permissible...' He said in al-Nahr: i.e., permissible rationally even if it does not occur. This is very far-fetched, and what makes it far-fetched is attributing permissibility to the statement, not to the answering, and there is no meaning to the disagreement on the permissibility of saying it rationally. So it is apparent that what is meant is legal permissibility. This is supported by his statement in Ghurar al-Adhkār: 'Mālik held it permissible to attend because his supplication may be answered in distress due to His statement: "When they board ships, they call upon Allah sincerely..." [29:65] and I say: and due to His statement: "He said, 'My Lord, give me respite until the Day they are raised.' He said, 'You are among the respited.'" [15:36] And perhaps this is the basis of what the fatwa is upon.'
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage addresses a subsidiary discussion: is it permissible to say that the supplication of a disbeliever is accepted? The commentator clarifies that the disagreement is about legal permissibility, not rational possibility. He quotes from al-Nahr that some understood it as rationally permissible, but he rejects that, saying the real issue is whether it is legally allowed to say that their supplication may be answered. He then cites Mālik’s opinion that it is permissible, based on the Quranic verse: disbelievers in distress call upon Allah sincerely. He adds another verse (Sūrat al-Ḥijr) where Iblīs’s supplication for respite was answered. He concludes that this is the basis of the fatwa.

Key Terms
يستجاب دعاء الكافرين (yustajābu du‘ā’ al-kāfirīn): The supplication of disbelievers is answered by Allah; this passage discusses the permissibility of stating this.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the permissibility of stating that the supplication of disbelievers may be accepted?
A) Consensus of the Companions.
B) The Quranic verse where disbelievers call upon Allah in distress.
C) The hadith that supplication is worship.
D) Rational necessity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits saying that a disbeliever's supplication may be accepted, based on Quranic evidence that Allah answers even disbelievers in distress.

Turning the Dying Person Towards Qibla
Explaining ruling and method of positioning dying person towards qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on positioning a dying person towards qibla and identify the primary sunnah method and the condition for leaving the person as is.

Core Idea
The dying person should be turned to face qibla on his right side; if difficult, he is left as he is.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling of tawjeeh al-muhtadar (turning the dying person towards qibla). It describes the signs of approaching death, the preferred method according to the transmitted sunnah (on the right side), and an alternative view held by some Hanafi scholars (on the back) for ease. The key principle is to facilitate the process without causing hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine what the passage is ruling on (turning the dying person towards qibla) and the legal status (sunnah, not wajib).
The matn uses the imperative 'لي' indicating recommendation.
2
Recognize the Primary Method
The transmitted sunnah (sunnah manqula) is to place the dying person on his right side facing qibla.
This is the established practice from the Prophet (peace be upon him).
3
Note the Alternative View
Some Hanafi scholars, especially from Transoxiana, preferred laying the person on his back with feet towards qibla, arguing it is easier for the soul's exit and for handling the body.
This view was criticized in Fath al-Qadir for lacking clear transmitted evidence.
4
Apply the Condition of Hardship
If turning the dying person causes significant difficulty or distress, he is left in his current position. The ruling is not to cause harm.
This is the ultimate principle: ease (taysir).
5
Summarize the Practical Ruling
The mufta bihi position is to attempt the right side first; if not possible, the back is acceptable; otherwise, leave as is.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولي المحتضر القبلة على يمينه) أي وجه وجه من حضره الموت فالمحتضر من قرب من الموت وعلامته أن يسترخي قدماه فلا ينتصبان وينعوج أنفه وينخسف صدغاه وتمتد جلدة الخصية لأن الخصية تتعلق بالموت وتتدلى جلدتها ولا يمتنع حضور الجنب والحائض وقت الاحتضار وإنما يوجه إلى القبلة على يمينه لأنه السنة المنقولة، واختار مشايخنا بما وراء النهر الاستلقاء على ظهره وقدماه إلى القبلة لأنه أيسر لخروج الروح. وتعقبه في فتح القدير وغيره بأنه لم يذكر فيه وجه ولم يعرف إلا نقلاً والله أعلم بالأيسر منهما ولكنه أيسر لتغميضه وشد لحيته وأمنع من تقوس أعضائه، ثم إذا ألقي على القفا يرفع رأسه قليلاً ليصير وجهه إلى القبلة دون السماء ا هـ . وفي المبتغى بالمعجمة والأصح أنه يوضع كما تيسر لاختلاف المواضع والأماكن ا.هـ. وهذا كله إذا لم يشق عليه، فإذا شق عليه ترك على حاله
His statement: (And let the dying person [be turned] towards the qibla on his right side) means turn the face of the one whom death has come. So the dying person (muḥtaḍar) is one who is near death. Its sign is that his feet relax and cannot stand, his nose becomes crooked, his temples sink, and the skin of his testicles stretches because the testicles hang at death and their skin dangles. The presence of a junub or menstruating woman is not prevented at the time of death. He is only turned towards the qibla on his right side because it is the transmitted sunnah. Our scholars in Transoxiana chose that he lie on his back with his feet towards the qibla, because it is easier for the soul's exit. It was criticized in Fatḥ al-Qadīr and others that no face was mentioned in it, and it is only known by transmission. And Allah knows best which is easier, but it [the back position] is easier for closing his eyes, tying his jaw, and preventing the curvature of his limbs. Then if he is placed on his back, his head is raised slightly so his face faces the qibla rather than the sky. End quote. And in al-Mubtaghā (with a 'jīm'), the most correct is that he is placed as is convenient, due to differing places and locations. End quote. All this is if it is not difficult for him; if it is difficult, he is left as he is.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage details the ruling of positioning a dying person (muḥtaḍar) towards the qibla. The matn states: 'ولي المحتضر القبلة على يمينه' — meaning the dying person should be turned to face the qibla lying on his right side. The commentary explains the signs of approaching death: feet go limp, nose distorts, temples sink, testicular skin stretches. The presence of a person in a state of major impurity (junub) or a menstruating woman is not prohibited at the time of death. The preferred method is on the right side (the transmitted sunnah). However, scholars from Transoxiana (Mā Warā' al-Nahr) preferred laying him on his back with feet towards the qibla, as it facilitates the soul's exit, the closing of eyes, tying the jaw, and prevents limbs from bending. Fatḥ al-Qadīr criticized this view for lacking clear evidence, but the author notes that whichever method is easier for the dying person should be adopted. If turning him causes difficulty, he is left in his current position.

Key Terms
محتضر (muḥtaḍar): One who is in the throes of death, near death
سنة منقولة (sunnah manqūlah): A transmitted practice from the Prophet (peace be upon him)
الاستلقاء (al-istilqā'): Lying on the back

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary sunnah method of positioning a dying person towards the qibla?
A) On his back with feet towards qibla
B) On his right side facing qibla
C) On his left side facing qibla
D) Sitting up facing qibla

Key Takeaway
The dying person should be turned to face qibla on his right side per sunnah, but if that causes hardship, he is left as he is; ease overrides.

Talqeen: Prompting the Shahada at Death
Ruling on prompting the dying person to say La ilaha illa Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talqeen, identify the primary hadith proof, and explain why it yields mustahabb rather than wujub.

Core Idea
Talqeen is recommended, not obligatory, because the hadith's indication is non-definitive (zanni).

When a person is dying, it is a sunnah to prompt them to say the shahada. But is this prompting an obligation or just a recommendation? The Hanafi school, as explained in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, carefully analyses the evidence to determine the legal weight. In this lesson, we will examine the hadith proof and the reasoning behind the conclusion that talqeen is mustahabb.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling from the matn
Start by identifying the ruling given in the base text: the dying person should be prompted to say the shahada but not commanded. The author considers it recommended (mustahabb).
The matn says 'ولقن الشهادة' without specifying degree; the commentary clarifies.
2
Identify the primary dalil
The author cites the authentic hadith: 'Whoever has his last words be La ilaha illa Allah will enter Paradise.' This is the main proof.
Hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah (indication)
The author argues that the hadith is an incitement (tahrid), not a command. The word 'dakhala' is a promise, not an imperative. Therefore, the indication is zanni (non-definitive), yielding recommendation, not obligation.
The author rejects the metaphorical interpretation of the other hadith 'Lqanu mawtakum', insisting on literal meaning.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Qunyah states that talqeen is wajib when death approaches. The author counters that it is mustahabb, because the command is not literal.
This shows how later Hanafi scholars settled the dispute.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
According to al-Mujtaba, once the dying person says it, it suffices unless he speaks again. The purpose is to make the shahada his last words.
Do not repeat incessantly; let the person reflect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولقن الشهادة بأن يقال عنده لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله ولا يؤمر بها للحديث الصحيح «من كان آخر كلامه لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنة» وهو تحريض على التلقين بها عند الموت فيفيد الاستحباب وحينئذ فلا حاجة إلى الاستدلال بالحديث الآخر «لقنوا موتاكم قول لا إله إلا الله» فإن حقيقته التلقين بعد الموت وقد اختلفوا فيه. وقولهم إنه مجاز تسمية للشيء باسم ما يؤول إليه قول لا دليل عليه لأن الأصل الحقيقة، وقد أطال المحقق في فتح القدير في رده. وفي المجتبى وإذا قالها مرة كفاه ولا يكثر عليه ما لم يتكلم بعد ذلك، ولما أكثر على ابن المبارك عن الوفاة قال : إذا قلت ذلك مرة فأنا على ذلك ما لم أتكلم لأن الغرض من التلقين أن يكون لا إله إلا الله آخر قوله ا هـ. وفي القنية: اشتد مرضه ودنا موته فالواجب على إخوانه وأصدقائه أن يلقنوه الشهادة ا هـ . وينبغي أن يكون مستحباً كما قدمناه لأن الأمر في الحديث لم يكن على حقيقته بل استعمل في مجازه فلم يكن الدلالة قطعي فلم يفد الوجوب.
His saying: (And he should be prompted to the shahada, i.e., one should say in his presence: 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah,' and he is not commanded to say it, due to the authentic hadith: 'Whoever has his last words be La ilaha illa Allah will enter Paradise.' This is an incitement to prompt him with it at death, so it indicates recommendation. Therefore, there is no need to cite the other hadith: 'Prompt your dying ones with the saying of La ilaha illa Allah,' for its literal meaning is prompting after death, and they differed concerning it. Their saying that it is a metaphor, naming a thing by its ultimate consequence, is a claim without evidence, because the default is literal meaning. The investigator in Fath al-Qadir elaborated in refuting it. In al-Mujtaba: If he says it once, it suffices, and he should not be made to repeat it unless he speaks after that. When it was said more than once to Ibn al-Mubarak about death, he said: 'If I said it once, I am upon that as long as I do not speak,' because the purpose of talqeen is that 'La ilaha illa Allah' be his last words. End. In al-Qunyah: If his illness intensifies and his death approaches, it is obligatory upon his brothers and friends to prompt him with the shahada. End. And it should be recommended, as we have stated, because the command in the hadith was not in its literal sense but was used metaphorically, so its indication is not definitive and thus does not necessitate obligation.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the talqeen, the prompting of the dying person to recite the shahada. The author first states the ruling from the matn: the dying person should be prompted to say 'La ilaha illa Allah, Muhammad Rasul Allah' but not commanded to say it. The proof is the authentic hadith that whoever has these as his last words enters Paradise. This hadith urges talqeen, indicating recommendation (istihbab), not obligation. The author then refutes the need to use the hadith 'Prompt your dying ones' as evidence for talqeen after death, explaining that its literal meaning is prompting after death, which is controversial. Some claim it is metaphorical, referring to the ultimate consequence, but the author rejects this, affirming that the default is literal meaning. The commentator in Fath al-Qadir extensively refutes that metaphorical interpretation. The passage then cites al-Mujtaba: if the dying person says it once, it suffices, and it should not be repeated unless he speaks again. This is based on the statement of Ibn al-Mubarak, who understood that the purpose is for the shahada to be his last words. Finally, al-Qunyah states that when illness becomes severe and death approaches, it is obligatory (wajib) upon the brothers and friends to prompt him. However, the author clarifies that this obligation is actually recommendation, because the command in the hadith is not literal but metaphorical, thus its indication is not definitive (qat'i), so it does not confer obligation (wujub).

Key Terms
تلقين (talqeen): The act of prompting the dying person to recite the shahada.
شهادة (shahada): The testimony of faith: 'La ilaha illa Allah, Muhammad Rasul Allah.'
استحباب (istihbab): Legal recommendation; an act whose performance is rewarded but omission is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal status of prompting the dying person (talqeen) according to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Mustahabb (recommended)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Talqeen is mustahabb; the Prophet's hadith indicates recommendation, not obligation, due to its metaphorical command.

6 min
Closing the Deceased's Eyes and the Hadith of the Soul
Ruling with proof and exegetical expansion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on closing the deceased's eyes, cite the hadith proof, and explain the two scholarly interpretations that resolve the apparent difficulty in the hadith.

Core Idea
Closing the deceased's eyes is recommended; the hadith 'the soul when taken, the sight follows it' has two subtle explanations.

This lesson explores a sunnah practice upon death: closing the eyes. The ruling is supported by a well-known hadith of Umm Salamah. However, the hadith raises a question: how can the eyes see after the soul departs? The Hanafi commentators offer two profound answers that reconcile the text with physical reality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The commentator states that closing the eyes of the deceased is a recommended (mustahabb) practice. This is the first ruling: it is sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah.
The Arabic text says 'يستحسن' meaning 'it is considered good'.
2
Locate the primary proof
The proof is the hadith of Umm Salamah, where the Prophet entered upon Abu Salamah after death, saw his eyes open, closed them, and said: 'Indeed, when the soul is taken, the sight follows it.'
The hadith is cited as evidence that the Prophet himself performed the act and gave a rationale.
3
Analyze the apparent difficulty
A literal reading suggests that after the soul leaves, the eyes should not see. This creates a contradiction. The author acknowledges this and offers a resolution after thirty years of reflection.
The difficulty is: how can the eyes follow something if they are already dead?
4
Understand the two resolutions
First resolution: The soul departs gradually; most leaves the body but some remains in the head and eyes, allowing sight until the soul fully exits. Second resolution: The soul retains a connection with the body after initial departure, so it can see, hear, and respond. Both explanations preserve the literal meaning.
The second view is supported by many scholars and provides evidence for the soul's continued connection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فإن مات شد الحياه وغمض عيناه بذلك جرى التوارث ثم فيه تحسينه فيستحسن وتقدم في الوضوء أن اللحي بفتح اللام منبت اللحية من الإنسان أو العظم الذي عليه الأسنان. وعن أم سلمة أن النبي دخل على أبي سلمة بعد الوفاة وقد شق بصره ثم قال : إن الروح إذا قبض تبعه البصر ثم قال: اللهم اغفر لأبي سلمة وارفع فأغمضه سيأتي قوله : (ثم قال إن الروح إذا قبض تبعه البصر) قال السيوطي في حاشيته على صحيح مسلم قال النووي : معناه إذا خرج الروح من الجسد تبعه البصر ناظراً أين تذهب قلت : وفي فهم هذا دقة فإنه قد يقال البصر إنما يبصر ما دام الروح في البدن فإذا فارقه تعطل الإبطار كما يتعطل الإحساس والذي ظهر لي فيه بعد النظر ثلاثين سنة أن يجاب بأحد أمرين أحدهما أن ذلك بعد خروج الروح من أكثر البدن وهي بعد باقية في الرأس والعينين فإذا خرج من الفم أكثرها ولم تنته كلها نظر البصر إلى القدر الذي خرج وقد ورد أن الروح على قدر أعضائه فإذا خرج بقيتها من الرأس والعين سكن النظر، فيكون قوله إذا قبض الروح معناه إذا شرع في قبضه ولم ينته قبضه الثاني أن يحمل على ما ذكره كثير من العلماء أن الروح لها اتصال بالبدن وإن كانت خارجة فترى وتسمع وترد السلام ويكون هذا الحديث من أقوى الأدلة على ذلك والله تعالى أعلم بمراد نبيه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم. وفي الروح لغتان التذكير والتأنيث كذا في شرح الباقاني قلت والجواب الثاني يرجع إلى ما ذكره النووي تدبر قوله : إلى أن يرفع أقول : الذي رأيته في النتف إلى أن يرفع إلى الغسل، وهكذا نقله عنها القهستاني لكن عبارة الزيلعي تكره القراءة عنده حتى يغسل ا هـ . وكذا قال في شرح المنية
His saying: (Then when he dies, he is shrouded and his eyes are closed. By this the transmission continued. Then, regarding its improvement, it is considered good. And it preceded in wudu that 'al-lahi' (with fatha on lam) means the root of the beard of a person or the bone on which the teeth are. And from Umm Salamah that the Prophet entered upon Abu Salamah after death, and his eyes were wide open, then he said: 'Indeed, when the soul is taken, the sight follows it.' Then he said: 'O Allah, forgive Abu Salamah and raise his degree...' Then his saying: (Then he said: 'Indeed, when the soul is taken, the sight follows it.') Al-Suyuti said in his gloss on Sahih Muslim, al-Nawawi said: Its meaning is when the soul departs from the body, the sight follows it, looking where it goes. I say: In understanding this there is subtlety, for it might be said that the sight only sees as long as the soul is in the body; when it separates, vision becomes disabled as sensation becomes disabled. What has become clear to me after thirty years of consideration is that it can be answered in one of two ways: first, that occurs after the soul has left most of the body but still remains in the head and eyes. So when most of it leaves from the mouth but not all, the sight looks at the part that has left. It has been narrated that the soul is distributed over the limbs. So when the remainder leaves from the head and eyes, the looking subsides. Thus his saying 'when the soul is taken' means when He begins to take it and has not finished taking it. Second, it can be interpreted as many scholars have mentioned: that the soul has connection with the body even when it is outside, so it sees, hears, and returns greetings. This hadith is among the strongest evidences for that. And Allah knows best the intent of His Prophet. And 'ruh' has two pronunciations: masculine and feminine, as in Sharh al-Baqani. I say the second answer refers to what al-Nawawi mentioned. Ponder his saying: 'until it is raised.' I say: What I saw in al-Nutaf: 'until it is raised to the washing.' Thus al-Qahastani quoted from it, but the wording of al-Zayla'i is that recitation is disliked near him until he is washed. End. And similarly said in Sharh al-Munyah.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning post-death actions, specifically closing the eyes of the deceased. The author comments on the matn's phrase 'and his eyes are closed.' He notes that this is a recommended practice (mustahabb) based on the hadith of Umm Salamah, where the Prophet closed the eyes of Abu Salamah after death and explained that the sight follows the soul when it is taken. The author then engages in a detailed exegetical discussion of the hadith, acknowledging a potential objection: if the soul leaves the body, how can the eyes see? He provides two possible answers after thirty years of contemplation. First, the soul leaves gradually; most of it exits first, but some remains in the head and eyes, allowing the eyes to see the departing part. Once the soul fully leaves, the eyes stop seeing. Second, as many scholars hold, the soul retains a connection with the body even after death, so it can see, hear, and respond. This hadith supports that view. The passage ends with a note on the point until which Quran should be recited: al-Nutaf says until the body is taken for washing, but al-Zayla'i says it is makruh to recite near him until he is washed. The author does not settle this dispute.

Key Terms
تغميض (taghmiid): The act of closing the deceased's eyes.
روح (ruh): The soul, which leaves the body at death.
قبض (qabd): The taking of the soul by the angel of death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's explanation, what is one possible interpretation of the hadith 'when the soul is taken, the sight follows it'?
A) The soul leaves instantly and the eyes see it in Paradise.
B) The soul leaves gradually; the eyes see the part that has exited until the soul fully departs.
C) The hadith is metaphorical and not to be taken literally.
D) The eyes continue to see after death permanently.

Key Takeaway
Closing the eyes of the deceased is a recommended sunnah, and the hadith about the soul and sight is understood through scholarly explanations that resolve its apparent difficulty.

Recommended Actions for the Dying and Placement on the Bier
List of recommended practices for the dying and post-death bier placement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the ten recommended actions for the dying and explain the recommended method for placing the deceased on a perfumed bier, including the ruling and the preferred orientation.

Core Idea
Ten highly recommended actions honor the dying; the bier is perfumed in odd numbers and placed as convenient.

In this lesson, we explore two critical aspects of end-of-life care: the sunan (recommended acts) for the dying person and the proper placement of the deceased on a perfumed bier. Understanding these practices ensures we fulfil the rights of the dying and deceased while following the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ten actions
Read through the list from al-Nutaf: turning to qibla, extending limbs, closing eyes, reciting Yasin, bringing a doctor, prompting shahada, removing women in impurity, placing a sword, reciting Quran, and hastening preparation.
The list is comprehensive and covers spiritual, medical, and ritual needs.
2
Classify their legal status
These are all mustahabb (sunnah ghayr muakkadah) – highly recommended but not obligatory. The evidence is from hadith and practice, not a direct obligation.
Common mistake: assuming they are fard or wajib.
3
Understand the evidence for hastening
The hadith 'Hasten with your dead' (عجلوا بموتاكم) is cited to emphasize speed in preparation and burial. This is a general recommendation.
The hadith applies to both righteous and sinful – the former benefits early, the latter removes burden.
4
Analyze the rulings for the perfumed bier
The bier should be perfumed with incense an odd number of times (1, 3, 5, or 7). There is a difference of opinion on the maximum (5 vs. 7); the author allows up to 7.
The orientation of the body is also disputed: lengthwise vs. widthwise. The preferred view is 'as convenient'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: perfume the bier with an odd number (up to 7) and place the body in whichever orientation is easiest. This accommodates practical needs.
The tarjih is based on flexibility and convenience, not strict prescription.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي النتف : يصنع بالمحتضر عشرة أشياء : يوجه إلى القبلة على قفاه أو يمينه، ويمد أعضاؤه، ويغمض عيناه، ويقرأ عند سورة يس»، ويحضر عنده من الطبيب، ويلقن لا إله إلا الله، ويخرج من عنده الحائض والنفساء والجنب، ويوضع على بطنه سيف لئلا ينتفخ، ويقرأ عنده القرآن إلى أن يرفع اهـ. أي إلى أن يرفع روحه. وفي التبيين: ويقول مغمضه الله وعلى ملة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، اللهم يسر عليه أمره وسهل عليه ما بعده وأسعده بلقائك واجعل ما خرج إليه خيراً مما خرج عنه. وفي المحيط : وليسرع في جهازه لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «عجلوا بموتاكم فإن يك خيراً قدمتموه إليه، وإن يك شراً فبعداً لأهل النار» قوله : ووضع على سرير مجمر وتراً) لئلا يعتريه نداوة الأرض ولينصب عنه الماء عند غسله، وفي التجمير تعظيمه وإزالة الرائحة الكريهة والوتر أحب إلى الله من غيره. وكيفيته أن يدار بالمجمرة حول السرير مرة أو ثلاثاً أو خمساً ولا يزاد عليها كذا في التبيين. وفي النهاية والكافي وفتح القدير : أو سبعاً ولا يزاد عليه وفي الظهيرية وكيفية الوضع عند بعض أصحابنا الوضع طولاً كما في حالة المرض إذا أراد الصلاة بإيماء، ومنهم من اختار الوضع عرضاً كما يوضع في القبر والأصح أنه يوضع كما تيسر ا هـ. وظاهر كلامه أن السرير يجمر قبل وضعه عليه وأنه يوضع عليه كما مات ولا يؤخر إلى وقت الغسل. وفي الغاية: يفعل
And in al-Nutaf: Ten things are done for the dying person: he is turned to face the qibla on his back or right side; his limbs are extended; his eyes are closed; Surah Yasin is recited near him; a doctor is brought to him; he is prompted with 'La ilaha illa Allah'; menstruating, postpartum, and junub women are removed from his presence; a sword is placed on his stomach to prevent bloating; the Quran is recited near him until he is raised—i.e., until his soul is raised. And in al-Tabyin: The one closing his eyes says: 'In the name of Allah and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah, O Allah, make his matter easy, facilitate what comes after, make him happy with Your meeting, and make what he has gone out to better than what he left behind.' And in al-Muhit: He should hasten his preparation, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Hasten with your dead, for if it is good, you have advanced him to it, and if it is evil, it is a distance for the people of the Fire.' His saying: (And he is placed on a bier perfumed with incense in an odd number) to prevent the dampness of the earth from affecting him and for the water to drain off when he is washed. Perfuming is for his honor and removal of bad odor, and odd numbers are more beloved to Allah. Its method is that the incense burner is passed around the bier once, three times, or five times, and not increased beyond that, as in al-Tabyin. And in al-Nihayah, al-Kafi, and Fath al-Qadir: or seven times and not increased. In al-Zahiriyyah: Regarding the method of placement, some of our companions say to place him lengthwise as in the state of illness when he intends to pray by gesture, and some choose to place him widthwise as he is placed in the grave. The most correct is that he is placed as is convenient. End. The apparent meaning of his statement is that the bier is perfumed before placing him on it, and that he is placed on it as he died, not delayed until the time of washing. And in al-Ghayah: he does...
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage presents a compilation of recommended actions for the dying person from the work al-Nutaf, followed by rulings on the placement of the deceased on a perfumed bier. The ten actions are: (1) turning him to face the qibla, either on his back or right side; (2) extending his limbs; (3) closing his eyes; (4) reciting Surah Yasin; (5) bringing a doctor; (6) prompting the shahada; (7) removing menstruating, postpartum, and junub women; (8) placing a sword on his stomach to prevent bloating; (9) reciting Quran until his soul is taken; (10) hastening the preparation (kafan and burial). The author then quotes a supplication to be said when closing the eyes from al-Tabyin. The hadith 'Hasten with your dead' is cited to emphasize speedy burial. The second part discusses the bier (sareer mujammar). The bier should be perfumed with incense an odd number of times (1, 3, 5, or 7) before placing the deceased on it. This is done to honor the deceased and eliminate odor. There is a difference of opinion on whether the body should be placed lengthwise (like a sick person praying) or widthwise (like in the grave). The author declares the most correct view to be that it is placed in whatever way is convenient. The bier is perfumed before placing the body, and the body is placed as it died, not delayed until washing.

Key Terms
محتضر (muhtadar): The person who is in the throes of death.
سرير مجمر (sareer mujammar): A bier that has been perfumed with incense.
تجمير (tajmeer): The act of perfuming with incense.
مغمض (mummidh): The one who closes the eyes of the deceased, and the supplication recited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the number of times to perfume the bier with incense?
A) Must be once only
B) Must be an odd number, up to seven
C) Must be an even number
D) Perfuming is not recommended

Key Takeaway
The dying and deceased are honoured through recommended practices (mustahabb), not obligations, with flexibility in bier placement to ease practical implementation.

Washing the Deceased: Procedure and Hanafi Differences
Detailed procedure and internal Hanafi disputes on washing the dead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah procedure for washing the deceased and identify the internal Hanafi disagreement on istinja' and the number of washings.

Core Idea
The sunnah is three washings with warm, cleansed water; the dispute over istinja' shows the precision of Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Washing the deceased is a communal obligation (fard kifayah), but the detailed method described in this passage is sunnah muakkadah. This commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the recommended procedure, the preferred water, and addresses subtle differences among the Hanafi imams, particularly regarding istinja' and the third washing. Understanding these details ensures proper practice and respect for the dead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling and sunnah aspects
Recognize that washing the deceased is fard kifayah, but the specific procedure detailed (water, number of washings, etc.) is sunnah muakkadah. Note the emphasis on using warm water with cleansers.
The author affirms hot water is better despite concerns about internal contents.
2
Trace the washing sequence
Follow the steps: after wudu-like ablution, wash head/beard with marshmallow, lay on left side for first wash, then right side for second, sit up and wipe belly, then lay on left again for third wash. Each 'wash' involves pouring water three times.
The third wash is sometimes not explicitly mentioned; the commentary clarifies it is part of the sunna.
3
Note the water preferences
The ideal water is boiled with lote leaves or soapwort; otherwise plain water. The first wash may be plain, second with cleanser, third with camphor according to some authorities.
Kawahirzad's specification is cited as an additional detail.
4
Identify the internal Hanafi difference on istinja'
There is disagreement: according to Abu Yusuf, istinja' (cleaning private parts) is not performed, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is. The author does not explicitly resolve this, but the mufta bihi may follow the majority.
This ikhtilaf is based on differing views on whether the deceased is subject to the same rules as the living.
5
Locate the ruling on applying perfume and camphor
Perfume (hanut) is placed on the head and beard, and camphor on the prostration points (forehead, nose, knees, etc.). Saffron is prohibited for males. This is sunna.
The prohibition of saffron is derived from the hadith forbidding men from wearing saffron in life.

عليه ماء مغلي بسدر أو حرض وإلا فالقراح وغسل رأسه ولحيته بالخطمي وأضجع على يساره فيغسل حتى يصل الماء إلى ما يلي التخت منه ثم على يمينه كذلك ثم أجلس مسنداً إليه ومسح بطنه رفيقاً وما خرج منه غسله ولم يعد غسله ونشف في ثوب وجعل الحنوط على رأسه ولحيته والكافور على مساجده ولا يسرح شعره ولحيته ولا...
بسدر هو عندنا، وهو ظاهر الرواية كالجنب وفي رواية لا فيهما لكنه لا يؤخر غسل رجليه في هذا الوضوء ولا يبدأ بغسل يديه بل بوجهه فخالف الجنب فيهما كذا في المحيط. ولم يذكر الاستنجاء للاختلاف فيه فعندهما يستنجي، وعند أبي يوسف لا . وأطلقه فشمل البالغ والصبي إلا أن الصبي الذي لا يعقل الصلاة لا يوضأ لأنه لم يكن بحيث يصلي قوله : (وصب عليه ماء مغلي أو حرض مبالغة في التنظيف لأن تسخين الماء كذلك مما يزيد في تحقيق المطلوب فكان مطلوباً شرعاً. وما يظن مانعاً وهو كون سخونته توجب انحلال ما في الباطن فيكثر الخارج لأن المقصود يتم إذ يحصل باستفراغ ما في الباطن تمام النظافة والأمان داع لا مانع من تلويث الكفن عند حركة الحاملين له فعندنا الماء الحار أفضل على كل حال. والحرض أشنان غير مطحون والمغلي من الإغلاء لا من الغلي والغليان لأنه لازم. كذا في المعراج قوله : (وإلا فالقراح) أي إن لم يتيسر ما ذكره فيصب عليه الماء الخالص لأن المقصود هو الطهارة ويحصل به قوله : وغسل رأسه ولحيته بالخطمي لأنه أبلغ في استخلاص الوسخ وإن لم يكن فبالصابون ونحوه لأنه يعمل عمله. هذا إذا كان في رأسه شعر اعتباراً بحالة الحياة. والخطمي بكسر الخاء نبت يغسل به الرأس كما في الصحاح ونقل القاضي عياض في تنبيهاته الفتح لا غير والمراد به خطمي العراق قوله : واضجع على يساره فيغسل حتى يصل الماء إلى ما يلي التخت منه ثم على يمينه كذلك لأن السنة البداءة من الميامن والمراد بما يلي التخت منه الجنب المتصل بالتخت والتخت بالخاء المعجمة لا بالحاء المهملة لأن بالحاء أن غسل ما يلي التخت المهملة يوهم الجنب لا الجنب المتصل بالتخت، أما بالخاء المعجمة يفهم الجنب المتصل . . ، كذا في معراج الدراية، وبه اندفع ما ذكره العيني من جواز الوجهين . قوله : (ثم اجلس مسنداً إليه ومسح بطنه رفيقاً وما خرج منه غسله تنظيفاً له . اعلم أن المصنف ذكر غسله مرتين : الأولى بقوله وأضجع على يساره فيغسل» الثانية بقوله ثم علي يمينه كذلك، ولم يذكر الغسلة الثالثة تمام السنة. قال في المحيط بعد إقعاده: ثم
