نفس من وجه وفي شرح المجمع للمصنف : إذا وضع المولود سقطاً تام الخلقة قال أبو يوسف : يغسل اكراماً لبني آدم. وقالا : يدرج في خرقة ولا يغسل، والصحيح قول أبي يوسف. وإذا لم يكن تام الخلق اجماعاً .اهـ. وبهذا ظهر ضعف ما في فتح القدير والخلاصة من السقط الذي لم تتم خلقة أعضائه المختار أنه يغسل اهـ . لما سمعت من الإجماع على عدم غسله قوله : (وفي الهداية أنه المختار فيه غفلة عن عبارة الهداية فإنها غير متعرضة للتسمية وعدمها . نعم في التبيين : واختلفوا في غسله وتسميته فذكر الكرخي عن محمد أنه لم يغسل ولم يسم، وذكر الطحاوي عن أبي يوسف أنه يغسل ويسمى ا.هـ. وفي الخانية والخلاصة والفيض والمجموع: وفي تسميته كلام قاله الشيخ إسماعيل قوله : ( ولعله سبق نظرهما الخ قال في النهر : ما في الخلاصة عزاه في الدراية إلى المبسوط والمحيط أفسبق نظر السرخسي وصاحب المحيط أيضاً كلا. وفي الظهيرية : السقط الذي لم تتم أعضاؤه لا يصلى عليه باتفاق الروايات، واختلفوا في غسله والمختار أنه يغسل ويدفن ملفوفاً بخرقة، وعزاه الشيخ إسماعيل إلى النهاية قال : وجزم به في عمدة المفتي والفيض والمجموع والخانية والمبتغى ثم قال : وبهذا يظهر ضعف ما في المنبع من أنه لا يغسل إجماعاً، وفي شرح ابن الملك وغرر الأذكار اتفاقاً، وما في البحر غير واضح بل الظاهر تضعيف الإجماع والاتفاق   ولعله سبق نظرهما الذي تم خلقه أو سهو من الكاتب . ثم اعلم أن قولهم هنا بأن من ولد ميتاً لا يرث ولا يورث ليس على إطلاقه لما في آخر الفتاوى الظهيرية من المقطعات: ومتى انفصل الحمل ميتاً إنما لا يرث إذا انفصل بنفسه، فأما إذا فصل فهو من جملة الورثة بيانه : إذا ضرب إنسان بطنها فألقت جنيناً ميتاً فهذا الجنين من جملة الورثة لأن الشارع أوجب على الضارب الغرة ووجوب الضمان بالجناية على الحي دون الميت فإذا حكمنا بحياته كان له الميراث ويورث عنه نصيبه كما يورث عنه بدل نفس وهو الغرة .اهـ. وهكذا في آخر المبسوط من ميراث الحمل. وفي المبتغى : السقط الذي لم تتم أعضاؤه هل يحشر؟ قيل : إذا نفخ فيه الروح يحشر وإلا فلا . وقيل : إذا استبان بعض خلقه يحشر اهـ وفي الظهيرية والذي يقتضيه مذهب علمائنا أنه إذا استبان بعض خلقه فإنه يحشر وهو قول الشعبي وابن سيرين اهـ .
And if he moves his eye. And the author mentioned that his ruling is to pray over him and it is required to wash him and that he inherits and is inherited from and that he is named even if he does not remain alive afterwards, out of honor because he is from the children of Adam, and it is possible that he has property that his father needs to mention his name when claiming it. And the author did not restrict by the existence of life in him until most of him comes out, but it is necessary. In al-Muhit: Abu Hanifa said: If some of the child comes out and moves then dies, if most of him came out, prayer is performed over him; if less came out, no prayer over him. etc. In al-Mubtagha: The child if his head comes out and he cries then dies before the rest comes out, he does not inherit and no prayer over him unless most of his body comes out alive; if a man slaughtered him while his head was coming out, he owes a ghurra; if he cut his ear and he came out alive then died, he owes full blood money. etc. In al-Mujtaba and al-Bada'i: They differed regarding istihlal (crying at birth). From Abu Hanifa: testimony of two men or one man and two women is not accepted regarding it, because crying and movement are observed by men. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the statement of women is accepted regarding it, except the mother, her statement is not accepted regarding inheritance by consensus because she is suspected of drawing benefit to herself. They accept women's statement because this scene is not attended by men. The statement of the midwife is accepted regarding the prayer in their opinion, and the mother is like the midwife as in al-Bada'i, but it is restricted by uprightness. They said: Because the report of a single person in religious matters is accepted if he is upright. etc. And since movement is evidence of life, they said: If a pregnant woman dies and in her belly is a child that moves, her belly is cut open and the child is taken out; nothing else suffices. Like that in al-Zahiriyya. And he indicated by his saying 'otherwise no' that if he does not cry out, no prayer is performed over him, and it follows that he is not washed, does not inherit, is not inherited from, and is not named. And they agreed on everything except washing and naming; they differed regarding them. The apparent position is that they are not done, and al-Tahawi reported doing them, and in al-Hidaya it is the chosen position because he is a soul in some respect. In Sharh al-Majma' of the author: If a woman gives birth to a perfectly formed stillborn, Abu Yusuf said: he is washed out of honor for the children of Adam. And the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?) said: he is wrapped in a cloth and not washed. The correct is the statement of Abu Yusuf. And if not perfectly formed, by consensus. etc. And by this the weakness of what is in Fath al-Qadir and al-Khulasa regarding the saqt (miscarriage) whose limbs are not fully formed, the chosen view that he is washed, becomes apparent. Because of the consensus you heard that he is not washed. His statement: (In al-Hidaya it is the chosen) contains heedlessness regarding the expression of al-Hidaya, for it does not address naming or its absence. Yes, in al-Tabyin: They differed regarding his washing and naming. Al-Karkhi reported from Muhammad that he is not washed and not named, and al-Tahawi reported from Abu Yusuf that he is washed and named. etc. In al-Khaniyya, al-Khulasa, al-Fayd, and al-Majmu': Regarding his naming there is a statement, said by Shaykh Isma'il. His statement: (And perhaps it was an oversight of both of them) etc. He said in al-Nahr: What is in al-Khulasa is attributed in al-Diraya to al-Mabsut and al-Muhit; then is it an oversight of al-Sarakhsi and the author of al-Muhit as well? No. In al-Zahiriyya: The saqt whose limbs are not complete, no prayer is performed over him by agreement of the narrations; they differed regarding his washing, and the chosen is that he is washed and buried wrapped in a cloth. Shaykh Isma'il attributed it to al-Nihaya and said it is stated decisively in 'Umdat al-Mufti, al-Fayd, al-Majmu', al-Khaniyya, and al-Mubtagha. Then he said: By this the weakness of what is in al-Munba' that he is not washed by consensus becomes apparent. In Sharh Ibn al-Malik and Ghurar al-Adhkar: by agreement. And what is in al-Bahr is not clear; rather the apparent is weakening of the consensus and agreement. And perhaps it was an oversight of both of them regarding the one whose creation is complete, or a scribal error. Then know that their statement here that one who is born dead does not inherit nor is inherited from is not absolute, because in the end of al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya from the muqatta'at: Whenever a fetus is born dead, he does not inherit only if he was born on his own; if he was expelled (by a blow), then he is among the heirs. Explanation: If a person strikes her belly and she miscarries a dead fetus, then this fetus is among the heirs because the Lawgiver imposed on the striker the ghurra, and the obligation of guarantee by the offense is upon the living, not the dead. So if we rule that he was alive, he has inheritance and his share is inherited from him, just as compensation for his soul, which is the ghurra, is inherited from him. etc. Similarly in the end of al-Mabsut regarding inheritance of pregnancy. In al-Mubtagha: Will the saqt whose limbs are not complete be resurrected? It is said: if the soul was blown into him, he will be resurrected, otherwise no. And it is said: if some of his creation became apparent, he will be resurrected. etc. In al-Zahiriyya: What the madhhab of our scholars necessitates is that if some of his creation became apparent, he will be resurrected, and it is the saying of al-Sha'bi and Ibn Sirin. etc.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage deals with the detailed rulings for a child born partially alive or stillborn. The author begins by stating that the ruling is to pray over the child, wash him, and that he inherits and is inherited from, and is named, even if he does not survive, out of honor for the human being. The key principle from Abu Hanifa, reported in al-Muhit, is that if most of the child's body emerges alive, then funeral prayer is performed; if less than half emerges, no prayer. The passage then discusses istihlal (crying at birth) as evidence of life. There is a dispute: Abu Hanifa requires two male witnesses or one man and two women, while the Sahibayn accept women's testimony except the mother's for inheritance due to suspected bias. The midwife's testimony is accepted regarding prayer. The text then addresses the case of a pregnant woman who dies: if the child moves, she must be cut open to save it. Next, the ruling for a child who dies after crying but before full emergence: no prayer or inheritance unless most of body emerged alive. The passage then details the consensus on the child not crying: no prayer, no wash, no inheritance, no naming, except differences on washing and naming. Some reports say wash and name (from Abu Yusuf), others do not. The preferred view in al-Hidaya is to wash but not necessarily name. The commentary then discusses the saqt (miscarriage) that is not perfectly formed: there is consensus that no prayer, but dispute over washing. The chosen view is to wash and bury in a cloth. Finally, the passage clarifies a common misconception: a child born dead due to external assault (e.g., a blow to the mother) does inherit because the Lawgiver treats him as alive for the purpose of the ghurra (compensation). The text ends with a note on resurrection: a saqt with some formed limbs will be resurrected according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الغرة (al-ghurra): Compensation paid for causing miscarriage, equal to one-tenth of a full diyah (blood money).
فصل (fassala): To expel; in the text, it refers to the fetus being forcibly expelled by a blow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a stillborn fetus inherit in the Hanafi school?
A) Always, because human life begins at conception
B) Never, because a dead person cannot inherit
C) Only if the death was caused by external assault
D) Only if the fetus is perfectly formed

Key Takeaway
A stillborn caused by assault inherits because the ghurra obligation legally treats the fetus as alive.

Four Categories of Disbelievers and the Validity of Their Conversion
Classification of disbelievers and conditions for valid conversion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a disbeliever into one of the four Hanafi categories and determine whether uttering the shahada suffices for their conversion.

Core Idea
The shahada suffices only when it negates what the person previously denied; for those who already affirm God's oneness, additional disavowal is required.

Converting to Islam is not a one-size-fits-all declaration. The Hanafi school recognizes that different types of disbelief require different statements to truly indicate a change of belief. This passage from al-Bada'i' classifies disbelievers into four categories and specifies when the shahada alone is sufficient and when more is needed. Understanding this classification helps avoid premature rulings on conversion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
List the four types of disbelievers as given: materialists (dahriyyah), dualists/Magians (thunawiyyah/majus), philosophers who deny prophethood, and Jews/Christians who deny Muhammad's prophethood.
These are not exhaustive but cover major groups.
2
Understand the specific denial of each category
For each category, note what they deny: the first denies the Creator, the second denies oneness, the third denies prophethood entirely, the fourth denies the particular prophethood of Muhammad.
This determines what statement will negate their disbelief.
3
Match the shahada to the denial
For categories 1 and 2, saying either 'La ilaha illallah' or the second shahada suffices because they previously rejected both divinity and oneness. For category 3, only the second shahada works since they already affirm God and oneness. For category 4, both shahadas together are not enough; they must also disavow their former religion.
The shahada must directly contradict the core denial.
4
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical
Take a person from category 2 (a Magian) who says 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan rasulullah'. Since he denies oneness, affirming prophethood is a sufficient indication of acceptance of Islam because he now accepts the message that includes tawhid.
The text explicitly says this suffices.
5
Recognize the exception for Jews and Christians
Even if they say both shahadas, they might still believe Muhammad was only sent to Arabs. Therefore, they must explicitly disavow their religion (e.g., say 'I disavow Judaism') to show they accept his universal prophethood.
This is a precautionary measure unique to the Hanafi school according to this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي مختصر أنفع الوسائل للزهيري عن البدائع : الكفار أضناف أربعة : صنف ينكرون الصانع وهم الدهرية، وصنف ينكرون الوحدانية وهم الثنوية والمجوس، وصنف يقرون بالصانع وتوحيده وينكرون الرسالة رأساً وهم قوم من الفلاسفة، وصنف يقرون بالصانع وتوحيده والرسالة في الجملة لكنهم ينكرون رسالة رسولنا عليه الصلاة والسلام وهم اليهود والنصارى. فإن كان من الأول الثاني فقال لا إله إلا الله يحكم بإسلامه، وكذلك إذا قال أشهد أن محمداً رسول الله لأنهم يمتنعون عن كل واحدة. وإن كان الثالث فقال من لا إله إلا الله لا يحكم بإسلامه، ولو قال أشهد أن محمداً رسول الله يحكم به لأنه يمتنع عن هذه فكان الإقرار بها دليل الإيمان وإن كان من الرابع فأتى بهما لا يحكم بإسلامه حتى يتبرأ عن الدين الذي هو عليه لأن من هؤلاء من يقر برسالة محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام لكنه يقول بعث إلى العرب دون غيرهم ا هـ . ملخصاً. ثم نقل عن قاضيخان أن في الذمي لا بد أن يقول أيضاً دخلت في دين الإسلام ثم ذكر أنه كما يصح الإسلام بالقول يصح بالفعل، وسمي . إيماناً بطريق الدلالة من أي من الأربعة كان كما إذا صلى بجماعة أو سجد للتلاوة أو أحرم وطاف أو صلى وحده أو أدى
And in Mukhtasar Anfa' al-Wasa'il by al-Zuhayri from al-Bada'i': The disbelievers are four categories: A category that denies the Creator, they are the materialists. A category that denies oneness, they are the dualists and the Magians. A category that affirms the Creator and His oneness but denies messengership entirely, they are a group of philosophers. And a category that affirms the Creator, His oneness, and messengership in general but denies the messengership of our Messenger (peace be upon him), they are the Jews and Christians. If he is from the first or second and says 'There is no god but Allah', he is judged to have entered Islam, and likewise if he says 'I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah', because they refrain from each one [of these statements]. If he is from the third and says 'There is no god but Allah', he is not judged to have entered Islam, but if he says 'I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah', he is judged [to have entered Islam] because he refrains from this [statement], so the affirmation is evidence of faith. If he is from the fourth and utters both [shahadas], he is not judged to have entered Islam until he disavows the religion he is upon, because among these are those who affirm the messengership of Muhammad (peace be upon him) but say he was sent to the Arabs only, etc., summarized. Then he transmitted from Qadikhan that for the dhimmi, he must also say 'I have entered the religion of Islam.' Then he mentioned that just as Islam is valid by speech, it is valid by action, and it is called faith by way of indication. From any of the four categories, such as if he prays in congregation, or prostrates in recitation (sajdat al-tilawah), or enters ihram and circumambulates [the Kaaba], or prays alone, or performs...
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage presents a classification of disbelievers from al-Bada'i' as quoted in Mukhtasar Anfa' al-Wasa'il. There are four types: (1) those who deny the Creator (materialists), (2) those who deny oneness (dualists and Magians), (3) those who affirm God and oneness but deny prophethood altogether (philosophers), and (4) those who affirm God, oneness, and prophethood in general but deny the prophethood of Muhammad (Jews and Christians). The ruling on conversion: For the first two types, saying 'La ilaha illallah' suffices because they previously denied both divinity and oneness; saying the shahada contradicts their belief. For the third type, saying 'La ilaha illallah' is not enough because they already affirm God and oneness; they must affirm Muhammad's prophethood by saying 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan rasulullah', since they denied prophethood. For the fourth type (Jews and Christians), even utter both shahadas is not enough; they must explicitly disavow their former religion (e.g., say 'I disavow Judaism/Christianity') because they might accept Muhammad as a prophet only for Arabs. Additionally, Islam can be valid by action (e.g., praying in congregation) as an indication of faith. The text also notes that a dhimmi needs to say 'I have entered the religion of Islam'. This classification helps determine when external utterances reflect genuine conversion.

Key Terms
الدهرية (al-dahriyyah): Materialists who deny the existence of a Creator.
الثنوية (al-thunawiyyah): Dualists, those who believe in two eternal principles (good and evil), e.g., Zoroastrians.
المجوس (al-majus): Magians, Zoroastrians, often categorized with dualists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A dualist (thunawi) says 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan rasulullah' but does not say the first shahada. According to the passage, is this sufficient for conversion?
A) Yes, because he affirmed prophethood.
B) No, because he must also say the first shahada.
C) Yes, because he is from category 2 and either shahada suffices.
D) No, because dualists must disavow dualism.

Key Takeaway
The validity of conversion via shahada depends on what belief it contradicts; for some, additional disavowal is required.

Duties toward a Deceased Non-Muslim Relative
States the ruling for a Muslim relative's duties toward a deceased non-Muslim relative

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four duties of a Muslim wali toward a deceased non-Muslim relative and explain the manner of carrying the bier.

Core Idea
A Muslim must wash, shroud, bury a non-Muslim relative and carry the bier legs-first.

This lesson extracts a clear ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the duties of a Muslim relative (wali) when a non-Muslim relative passes away. The text specifies four obligations: washing, shrouding, burying, and carrying the bier in a particular manner. Understanding this ruling is essential for fulfilling the rights of kinship even across religious boundaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Actor
Who is obligated? The text says 'ولي مسلم' – a Muslim guardian (wali). The wali is typically the closest Muslim relative (heir or custodian). Determine who that is in your own family context.
If no Muslim relative, the duty may shift to the Muslim community.
2
List the Actions
The text mentions three actions: يغسل (washes), يكفن (shrouds), يدفن (buries). These are sequential duties. Note that prayer (salat al-janazah) is not included for a non-Muslim.
3
Analyze the Manner of Carrying
The phrase 'ويؤخذ سريره بقوائمه' means the bier (سرير) is taken by its legs (بقوائمه). This indicates that during transportation, the legs should be carried first (or the bier is carried feet forward). This is a specific sunnah in burial rites.
Some scholars interpret this as a mark of respect, others as a practical measure.
4
Determine the Legal Status
The ruling is a command (wujub). According to the Hanafi school, it is wajib upon the Muslim wali to perform these acts, provided it does not cause harm or involve prohibited acts (like reciting Quran at the burial). The absence of these duties would be a sin.
The ruling applies to a non-Muslim relative who is not a harbi (enemy combatant).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويغسل ولي مسلم الكافر ويكفنه ويدفنه ويؤخذ سريره بقوائمه
The Muslim guardian washes the disbeliever, shrouds him, buries him, and his bier is taken by its legs.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It states the obligations of a Muslim relative (wali) towards a deceased non-Muslim relative. The wali must wash, shroud, and bury the deceased. Additionally, the bier should be carried by its legs (i.e., the legs go first when carrying). This ruling applies when the deceased is a relative who has not embraced Islam.

Key Terms
ولي (wali): Guardian or responsible relative (often the heir or nearest kin).
سرير (sarir): Bier or stretcher on which the deceased is carried.
قوائم (qawa'im): Legs (of the bier or of the deceased). Here it means the bier is carried by its legs, i.e., feet first.
كافر (kafir): Disbeliever; one who rejects Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding a Muslim's duty towards a deceased non-Muslim relative?
A) No need to perform any rites
B) Wash, shroud, and bury
C) Only bury
D) Only wash and pray janazah

Key Takeaway
A Muslim wali must wash, shroud, and bury a deceased non-Muslim relative, carrying the bier feet-first, but without janazah prayer.

Conditions for Accepting Islam Based on Prior Beliefs
Explains how to judge Islam of a convert based on prior belief category

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of disbelievers and apply the Hanafi rule for judging Islam based on the convert's prior beliefs.

Core Idea
The sufficiency of the shahada depends on what the convert previously denied.

This lesson unpacks a key Hanafi ruling: not all declarations of faith are treated equally. The school considers what the person previously rejected. For atheists, saying 'La ilaha illa Allah' suffices. For those who denied prophethood, accepting Muhammad (PBUH) is key. For Jews and Christians, they must also explicitly disavow their prior religion. This nuanced approach demonstrates the Hanafi commitment to assessing inner conviction and the practical implications for judging conversion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
List the four groups: atheists (dahriyya), dualists (thanawiyya/majus), deniers of prophethood (philosophers), and People of the Book (Jews/Christians).
This classification is from al-Bada'i' by al-Kasani.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each category
For first two: saying 'La ilaha illa Allah' is sufficient. For third: saying 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasulu Allah' is sufficient. For fourth: both shahadas plus explicit disavowal of prior religion are required.
The ruling is based on what each group denied.
3
Follow the reasoning (talil)
Each category rejected a specific aspect of faith. Acknowledging that aspect proves conversion. For atheists and dualists, they denied the existence/oneness of God, so uttering the first part of the shahada is enough. For deniers of prophethood, they rejected messengerhood, so testifying to Muhammad's prophethood suffices. For People of the Book, they already affirm God and prophethood in general, so they must specifically accept Muhammad and reject their former faith.
This is a logical application of the principle that acknowledgment of what one previously denied indicates a change of belief.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
A Jew who says both parts of the shahada but does not disavow Judaism is not considered Muslim. This differs from other schools that might accept a general declaration.
The Hanafi view is upheld in this text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يوجب الحكم بالإسلام ما لم يؤمن بما ذكرنا وعلى هذا قالوا لو اشترى جارية أو تزوّج امرأة فاستوصفها صفة الإسلام فلم تعرفه لا تكون مسلمة. والمراد من عدم المعرفة ليس ما يظهر من التوقف في جواب ما الأيمان ما الإسلام كما يكون من بعض العوام لقصورهم في التعبير بل قيام الجهل بذلك بالباطن مثلاً بأن البعث هل يوجد أو لا، وأن الرسل وإنزال الكتب عليهم كان أو لا، لا يكون في اعتقاده اعتقاد طرف الإثبات للجهل البسيط فعن ذلك قالت لا أعرفه، وقل ما يكون ذلك لمن نشأ في دار الإسلام فإنا نسمع ممن قد يقول في جواب ما قلنا لا أعرف وهو من التوحيد والإقرار والخوف من النار وطلب الجنة بمكان، بل وذكر ما يصلح استدلالاً في أثناء أحوالهم وتكلمهم على التصريح ما يصرح باعتقاد هذه الأمور وكانوا يظنون أن جواب هذه الأشياء إنما يكون بكلام خاص منظوم وعبارة عالية حاجة فيحجمون عن الجواب .اهـ. فعلى هذا فينبغي أن لا يسأل العامي والمرأة على هذا الوجه بأن يقال ما الأيمان، وإنما يذكر حقيقة الإيمان وما يجب الإيمان به بحضرتهما، ثم يقال له هل أنت مصدق بهذا فإذا قال نعم كان ذلك كافياً. وأفاد بقوله . (أو لم يسب أحدهما معه أنه يصلي عليه إذا دخل دار الإسلام ولم يكن معه أحد أبويه تبعاً لدار الإسلام وفي التبيين أي إذا لم يسب مع الصبي أحد أبويه فحينئذ يصلى عليه تبعاً للسابي أو الدار اهـ. فجعل كلام المصنف شاملاً لتبعية السابي ولتبعية الدار، والظاهر أنه لم يتعرض لتبعية السابي فإن السبي في اللغة الأسر والسبي الأسرى المحمولون من بلد إلى بلد. وفي مختصر أنفع الوسائل للزهيري عن البدائع : الكفار أضناف أربعة : صنف ينكرون الصانع وهم الدهرية، وصنف ينكرون الوحدانية وهم الثنوية والمجوس، وصنف يقرون بالصانع وتوحيده وينكرون الرسالة رأساً وهم قوم من الفلاسفة، وصنف يقرون بالصانع وتوحيده والرسالة في الجملة لكنهم ينكرون رسالة رسولنا عليه الصلاة والسلام وهم اليهود والنصارى. فإن كان من الأول الثاني فقال لا إله إلا الله يحكم بإسلامه، وكذلك إذا قال أشهد أن محمداً رسول الله لأنهم يمتنعون عن كل واحدة. وإن كان الثالث فقال من لا إله إلا الله لا يحكم بإسلامه، ولو قال أشهد أن محمداً رسول الله يحكم به لأنه يمتنع عن هذه فكان الإقرار بها دليل الإيمان وإن كان من الرابع فأتى بهما لا يحكم بإسلامه حتى يتبرأ عن الدين الذي هو عليه لأن من هؤلاء من يقر برسالة محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام لكنه يقول بعث إلى العرب دون غيرهم ا هـ . ملخصاً. ثم نقل عن قاضيخان أن في الذمي لا بد أن يقول أيضاً دخلت في دين الإسلام ثم ذكر أنه كما يصح الإسلام بالقول يصح بالفعل، وسمي إيماناً بطريق الدلالة من أي من الأربعة كان كما إذا صلى بجماعة أو سجد للتلاوة أو أحرم وطاف أو صلى وحده أو أدى زكاة الإبل أو أذن في وقت الصلاة
He judges Islam unless he believes what we mentioned. Based on this, they said: if one buys a slave girl or marries a woman and asks her about the attribute of Islam and she does not know it, she is not a Muslim. And what is meant by lack of knowledge is not what appears from hesitation in answering 'what is faith' as happens with some common people due to their inability to express, but rather the existence of ignorance in the inner self, for example, whether the resurrection exists or not, and whether messengers and books were sent or not, so that he does not have belief in the affirmative due to simple ignorance. For that reason, she said 'I do not know it'. And rarely does that happen for one raised in the abode of Islam, for we hear from one who may say in answer to what we said 'I do not know' while he is well-versed in tawhid, acknowledgment, fear of the Fire, and desire for Paradise. Rather, he mentions what can be used as evidence in their situations and their speech, while they express belief in these matters, but they think that the answer to these things requires special composed words and high expressions, so they refrain from answering. End quote. Based on this, one should not ask the common person and the woman in this manner, saying 'what is faith', but rather mention the reality of faith and what must be believed in their presence, then ask him 'do you affirm this?'. If he says yes, that is sufficient. And he benefited by his saying: (or neither of the two parents precedes him...) that he prays over him if he enters the abode of Islam and neither of his parents is with him, following the abode of Islam. And in al-Tabyin: if neither parent of the child is captured with him, then he is prayed over following the captor or the abode. End. So he made the author's words inclusive of following the captor and following the abode. The apparent is that he did not address following the captor, for 'sabi' in language means captivity and 'sabi' are the captives transported from land to land. And in the abridged 'Anfa' al-Wasa'il' by al-Zuhayri from al-Bada'i': The disbelievers are four categories: a category that denies the Creator, they are the Dahriyya; a category that denies monotheism, they are the Dualists and Zoroastrians; a category that affirms the Creator and His oneness but denies messengerhood entirely, they are a group of philosophers; and a category that affirms the Creator, His oneness, and messengerhood in general but denies the messengerhood of our Messenger (peace be upon him), they are the Jews and Christians. If he is from the first or second and says 'La ilaha illa Allah', he is judged as Muslim, and likewise if he says 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasulu Allah' because they refrain from each one. If he is from the third and says 'La ilaha illa Allah', he is not judged as Muslim, but if he says 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasulu Allah', he is judged because he refrains from this, so acknowledgment of it is evidence of faith. If he is from the fourth and utters both, he is not judged as Muslim until he disavows the religion he was upon, because among these are those who affirm the messengerhood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) but say he was sent to the Arabs only. End summary. Then he narrated from Qadikhan that regarding the dhimmī, he must also say 'I have entered the religion of Islam'. Then he mentioned that just as Islam is valid by speech, it is also valid by action, and is called faith by implication from whichever of the four categories it is, such as if he prays in congregation, prostrates for tilawah, enters ihram and performs tawaf, prays alone, pays zakat on camels, or gives the adhan at the time of prayer.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the conditions for accepting a person's declaration of Islam. It first discusses the situation where a person claims ignorance of the fundamentals of faith. The author clarifies that genuine ignorance (jahl basit) is different from an inability to articulate. For common people, they should not be asked formal theological questions but rather presented with the truth and asked if they affirm it. Then the text discusses the four categories of disbelievers as mentioned in al-Bada'i' (by al-Kasani). For each category, the effect of uttering the shahada differs. For atheists and polytheists, saying 'La ilaha illa Allah' alone is sufficient. For those who believe in God but deny prophethood, they need to accept Muhammad as the Messenger. For Jews and Christians, they must also explicitly disavow their previous religion. Finally, the passage notes that even without speech, actions indicative of Islam (like performing salah or giving zakat) can also establish faith.

Key Terms
دهرية (dahriyya): Those who deny the existence of a creator, atheists
ثنوية (thanawiyya): Dualists who believe in two gods
مجوس (majus): Zoroastrians, often considered dualists

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a Jew says both 'La ilaha illa Allah' and 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasulu Allah', is he considered Muslim?
A) Yes, immediately
B) No, not until he disavows his prior religion
C) Only if he says it in Arabic
D) Only if he prays

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school judges conversion by considering what the convert previously denied; for Jews and Christians, explicit disavowal of their former religion is required.

Accepting Common People's Faith and Actions as Evidence of Islam
Provides method for accepting faith of common people and actions as evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method for accepting a common person's declaration of faith and identify actions that serve as evidence of Islam.

Core Idea
Common people should be asked to affirm faith simply, and actions can establish Islam even without words.

This lesson covers two practical topics from the passage: How to properly accept the Islam of a common person who may struggle to articulate faith, and how certain actions—like praying or giving zakat—can be sufficient evidence of conversion. The Hanafi school shows flexibility in evaluating faith, focusing on inner conviction and public practice rather than precise wording.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish genuine ignorance from inarticulacy
A person who hesitates to answer 'what is faith?' may not be ignorant but simply unable to express it. The text warns against assuming disbelief.
The passage gives an example of common people who are actually believers but cannot formulate formal answers.
2
Apply the correct method of questioning
Instead of asking abstract questions, explain the essentials of faith and ask 'Do you affirm this?' A simple 'yes' is sufficient.
This is from the author's recommendation after quoting earlier scholars.
3
Identify actions that imply Islam
Actions such as praying in congregation, prostrating for tilawah, performing tawaf, paying zakat, or giving adhan are public demonstrations of faith.
These actions are mentioned in the latter part of the passage.
4
Understand the ruling on actions
Such actions make the person Muslim by implication (dalalah). They are valid indications of faith regardless of the person's prior category.
The text says 'كما يصح الإسلام بالقول يصح بالفعل'.

Standing at the Grave During Burial: Sunnah and Permissibility
Ruling with proof on standing at the grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing at the grave while the soil is being leveled and explain the evidence for both standing and sitting.

Core Idea
Standing at the grave is sunnah until the earth is leveled; sitting becomes permissible after placement.

When a loved one is buried, what should those present do? This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the preferred action: standing at the grave until the soil is leveled, following the Prophet's practice. However, a later hadith shows that sitting is permissible after the body is placed in the niche, especially to avoid resembling non-Muslim practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses standing (qiyam) at the grave while the earth is being filled. What is the preferred ruling? The author states it is 'better' (الأفضل) not to sit until the soil is leveled, indicating sunnah.
The term 'الأفضل' typically indicates a sunnah or mustahabb ruling.
2
Locate the first dalil
The first proof: the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to stand until the earth was leveled over the deceased. This shows standing is a recommended act.
Hadith: 'He used to stand until the soil was leveled over him.'
3
Note the second dalil (Ubadah)
The second proof: the Prophet sat after the body was placed in the niche to oppose a Jew who said their dead stand. This indicates permissibility of sitting after placement.
This hadith is from Ubadah ibn al-Samit and provides a concession.
4
Distinguish the two situations
The two hadiths apply at different times: standing before the grave is filled, sitting after placement. The author gives precedence to the first (standing) as superior, but acknowledges the second.
The key is timing: before vs after placement.
5
Apply the final nuance
The passage adds that those not actively following the funeral (e.g., passersby) need not stand. The mufta bihi is to stand until the earth is leveled for those accompanying the funeral.
This is based on a narration from Ali and the ruling in al-Zahiriyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأفضل أن لا يجلسوا مالم يسووا عليه التراب لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يقوم حتى يسوى عليه التراب، ولأن في القيام إظهار العناية بأمر الميت وأنه مستحب اهـ. والأولى الأول لما في البدائع : فأما بعد الوضع فلا بأس بالجلوس لما روي عن عبادة بن الصامت أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان لا يجلس حتى يوضع الميت في اللحد فكان قائماً مع أصحابه على رأس قبر فقال يهودي : هكذا نصنع بموتانا فجلس صلى الله عليه وسلم وقال لأصحابه : خالفوهم اهـ. أي في القيام فلذاكره. وقيدنا بمتبعها لأن من لم يرد اتباعها ومرت عليه فالمختار أنه لا يقوم لها لما روي عن علي رضي الله عنه كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا أمرنا بالقيام في الجنازة ثم جلس بعد ذلك وأمرنا بالجلوس بهذا اللفظ لأحمد رحمه الله، وصحح في الظهيرية أن من في المصلى لا يقوم لها إذا رآها قبل أن توضع.
And it is better that they do not sit until the soil is leveled over him, due to the narration that he (peace be upon him) used to stand until the soil was leveled over him, and because standing shows care for the deceased's matter and it is recommended. And the first is better due to what is in al-Bada'i': 'As for after placement, there is no harm in sitting because of the narration from Ubadah ibn al-Samit that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would not sit until the deceased was placed in the niche, and he was standing with his companions at the head of a grave, so a Jew said, "We do this with our dead," so he sat down and said to his companions, "Oppose them." That is, in standing, so remember that. And we restricted it to the follower because whoever does not intend to follow and it passes him, the chosen view is that he does not stand for it, due to the narration from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not command us to stand at the funeral, then afterwards he sat and commanded us to sit. With this wording from Ahmad (may Allah have mercy on him). And it is authenticated in al-Zahiriyyah that whoever is in the prayer hall does not stand for it if he sees it before it is placed.'
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on standing at the grave while the soil is being leveled. The preferred view is to stand, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to do, showing care for the deceased. However, after the body is placed in the niche, sitting is permissible based on another hadith where the Prophet sat to oppose the Jews who stood for their dead. The author prioritizes the first view (standing) as superior, but notes that the ruling varies depending on intention. For those not actively following the funeral, the relied-upon position is that they do not need to stand. The passage clarifies that the sunnah is not to sit until the grave is filled, but concession is given after placement.

Key Terms
القيام (al-qiyam): Standing at the grave while it is being filled.
الجلوس (al-julus): Sitting after the deceased has been placed in the niche.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Walking Behind the Bier: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute with Shafi'i on walking in front vs behind the funeral bier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on walking behind the funeral bier and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the concept of intercession.

Core Idea
Mourners are followers (مشيعون), not intercessors to prepare the way; hence they walk behind the bier.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the Hanafi ruling on the position of mourners in a funeral procession. The author contrasts the Hanafi view with the Shafi'i view and provides the rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State the Hanafi ruling: walking behind the bier is sunnah muakkadah; walking in front is makruh tanzih if too far or all go ahead.
2
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the intercessor (شفيع) should go ahead to prepare the matter, analogizing to the imam in prayer.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis distinguish between intercession in prayer (where the imam leads) and walking in the procession (where mourners follow). The deceased is not present for intercession during the walk.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi transmission
Note the report from Abu Yusuf that Abu Hanifa rode ahead, but this is from al-Nawadir and not the relied-upon view (mufta bihi).
5
Clarify the ruling on riding and walking
Riding is permitted but walking is better. The dislike for walking in front is tanzih (makruh tanzih), not tahrimi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هم شفعاء قوله (ومشى قدامها أي بلا مشي لمتبعها أمامها لأن المشي خلفها أفضل عندنا للأحاديث الواردة باتباع الجنائز، وقد نقل فعل السلف على الوجهين والترجيح بالمعنى، فالشافعي يقول والشفيع يتقدم ليمهد المقصود، ونحن نقول هم مشيعون فيتأخرون والشفيع المتقدم هو الذي لا يستصحب المشفوع له في الشفاعة وما نحن فيه بخلافه، بل قد ثبت شرعاً إلزام تقديمه حالة الشفاعة له أعني حالة الصلاة فثبت شرعاً عدم اعتبار ما اعتبره. قالوا: ويجوز المشي أمامها إلا أن يتباعد عنها أو يتقدم الكل فيكره ولا يمشي عن يمينها ولا عن شمالها . وذكر الأسبيجابي : ولا بأس بأن يذهب إلى صلاة الجنازة راكباً غير أنه يكره له التقدم أمام الجنازة بخلاف الماشي .اهـ. وبهذا يضعف ما نقله ابن الملك في شرح المجمع معزياً إلى أبي يوسف فقال : رأيت أبا حنيفة يتقدم الجنازة وهو راكب ثم قعد حتى تأتيه . كذا في النوادر اهـ. وفي الظهيرية والمشي فيها أفضل من الركوب كصلاة الجمعة. وفي الغاية : اتباع الجنائز أفضل من النوافل إذا كان الجوار أو قرابة أو صلاح مشهور وإلا فالنوافل أفضل. قوله : فلذا كره يفيد أن قول البدائع «فلا بأس بالجلوس» ليس جارياً . ما الغالب في استعماله فيما تركه أولى قوله : قالوا ويجوز المشي أمامها إلا أن يتباعد الخ) قال الرملي : الظاهر أنها كراهة تنزيه وكذا ما بعده.
They are intercessors. His saying: 'And he walked in front of it' i.e., without walking for its follower in front of it, because walking behind it is better in our school due to the hadiths about following funerals, and the action of the Salaf has been transmitted on both sides, and the preference is based on meaning. Al-Shafi'i says: The intercessor comes forward to prepare the intended matter, and we say: They are followers, so they stay behind. The forward intercessor is the one who does not take the one for whom he intercedes along in the intercession, and our case is otherwise. Rather, it has been established by Shariah that he must be brought forward at the time of intercession for him, i.e., at the time of prayer, so it is established by Shariah that what he considered is not considered. They said: And walking in front of it is permissible unless he distances himself from it or all of them go ahead, then it is disliked, and he should not walk on its right nor on its left. And al-Asbijabi mentioned: There is no harm in going to the funeral prayer riding, except that it is disliked for him to go ahead of the funeral, unlike the walker. This weakens what Ibn al-Malik transmitted in Sharh al-Majma' attributed to Abu Yusuf, who said: I saw Abu Hanifa go ahead of the funeral while riding, then he sat until it came to him. This is in al-Nawadir. And in al-Zahiriyyah: Walking in it is better than riding, like the Friday prayer. And in al-Ghayah: Following funerals is better than supererogatory prayers if it is a neighbor, relative, or well-known pious person; otherwise, supererogatory prayers are better. His saying: 'Thus it is disliked' indicates that the statement of al-Bada'i' 'there is no harm in sitting' is not operative. What is predominantly used is in what is better to leave. His saying: 'They said: And walking in front of it is permissible unless he distances himself...' al-Ramli said: The apparent is that it is tanzih dislike, and likewise what follows.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on walking at a funeral. Unlike the Shafi'i view that the intercessor (the leader) should walk ahead, Hanafis hold that the followers should walk behind the bier, as they are interceding but not taking the deceased along. Walking in front is permitted if not too far, but disliked if all move ahead. Riding is allowed but walking is better. A narration that Abu Hanifa rode ahead is considered weak. The passage also clarifies that the dislike (karahah) is tanzihi, not tahrimi.

Key Terms
مشيعون (mushayyi'un): Followers, mourners attending the funeral procession.
شفيع (shafi'): Intercessor; here referring to the leader of the funeral prayer or the one leading the procession.
كراهة تنزيه (karahah tanzih): Disliked but not sinful (makruh tanzihi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where should the mourners walk in relation to the funeral bier?
A) In front of the bier
B) Behind the bier
C) On the right side
D) On the left side

Key Takeaway
Mourners are followers (مشيعون), so they walk behind the bier; the Shafi'i analogy of the intercessor does not apply to the procession.

Burial Procedures: Walking Around the Bier and Digging the Grave
Brief instructions for positioning and grave preparation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended order of carrying the bier and describe the Hanafi sunnah of digging a niche (lahd).

Core Idea
Begin on the right, then back, front on left, then back; dig a niche (lahd) for the deceased.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides concise instructions for the burial of the deceased. It covers the order in which bearers should position themselves around the bier and the method of preparing the grave by digging a niche (lahd). Understanding these rites ensures proper performance of the funeral according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The passage describes the order of walking around the bier and the subsequent digging of the grave with a niche. Recognize that this is a sunnah procedure.
2
Memorize the order
The order is: begin on the right side, then the back, then the front on the left, then the back again. This may refer to the bearers' positions around the bier.
The text uses 'its' referring to the bier.
3
Note the burial actions
After the procession, the grave is dug and a niche (lahd) is made on the side facing the qibla. The body is entered from the niche side.
Lahd is sunnah; if ground is hard, a shaqq (trench) is allowed.
4
Understand the legal ruling
These actions are sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory. The burial itself is fard kifayah, but the specific order and lahd are recommended.
Omitting them does not invalidate the burial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يمينك ثم مؤخرها ثم مقدمها على يسارك ثم مؤخرها ويحفر القبر ويلحد ويدخل من
Your right then its back then its front on your left then its back, and he digs the grave and makes a niche and enters from
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This very brief passage describes the order of walking around the bier (likely placing it in the grave) and the burial process: first the right side, then the back, then the front on the left, then the back again. It also mentions digging the grave, making a niche (لحد), and entering from there. This is a concise instruction for the burial procedure, probably meant to be memorized.

Key Terms
اللحد (al-lahd): The niche dug in the side of the grave to place the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Left
B) Back
C) Right
D) Front

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah for burial includes starting the procession on the right side and digging a niche (lahd) in the grave.

Rulings for Funeral Participants: Following to Prayer and Women's Prohibition
Two rulings: staying for prayer and women's prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that it is wajib to follow the funeral until the prayer and that women's attendance is haram, and cite the hadith as proof.

Core Idea
The purpose of following the funeral is the prayer; women are forbidden from attending.

The passage begins with a clear rule: one should follow the funeral procession until the Janazah prayer is completed. It then addresses the issue of women's attendance, providing a direct prophetic prohibition. This lesson analyzes both rulings and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Read the first sentence: 'يتبع جنازة حتى يصلي'. The act is following the funeral. The ruling is that one must continue until the prayer.
The reason given: 'لأن الاتباع كان للصلاة عليها'.
2
Locate the Dalil for Women's Attendance
The text quotes the Prophet's statement: 'انصرفن مأزورات غير مأجورات' (Return, you are sinful, not rewarded). This is a clear prohibition.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The phrase 'مأزورات' (sinful) indicates that the act incurs sin, thus it is haram. The prohibition is explicit.
The Hanafi usul rule: explicit prohibition indicates haram.
4
Note the Cross-Madhhab Ikhtilaf
Some schools of thought allow women to attend under certain conditions. The Hanafi position is strict prohibition based on this hadith.
The thamarah al-khilaf: women do not attend in Hanafi practice.
5
Apply the Ruling
In practice, women should not go to funerals. If they do, they commit a sin. The sunnah of following is not abandoned due to their presence.
The later part of the passage addresses if a hired wailer is present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يتبع جنازة حتى يصلي لأن الاتباع كان للصلاة عليها فلا يرجع قبل حصول المقصود. ولا ينبغي للنساء أن يخرجن في الجنازة لأن النبي الله نهاهن عن ذلك وقال: انصرفن مأزورات غير مأجورات. ويكره النوح والصياح في الجنازة ومنزل الميت للنهي عنه، فأما البكاء فلا بأس به. وإن كان مع الجنازة نائحة أو صائحة زجرت، فإن لم تنزجر فلا بأس بأن تتبع الجنازة ولا يمتنع لأجلها لأن الاتباع سنة فلا تترك ببدعة من غيره اهـ. وفي المجتبى قال البقالي : إذا استمع إلى باكية ليلين فلا بأس إذا أمن الوقوع في الفتنة لاستماعه عليه الصلاة والسلام لبواكي حمزة ولا تتبع بنار في مجمرة ولا شمع ولا بأس بمرثية الميت، شعراً كان أو غيره.
He follows the funeral until he prays, because following was for the prayer upon her, so he should not return before achieving the purpose. And it is not proper for women to go out at the funeral because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade them from that and said: 'Return, you are sinful, not rewarded.' And wailing and screaming in the funeral and the house of the deceased are disliked due to the prohibition. As for crying, there is no harm in it. And if there is a woman wailing or screaming with the funeral, she is rebuked; if she does not desist, then there is no harm in following the funeral and it is not prevented because of her, because following is a sunnah, so it is not abandoned due to a bid'ah of someone else. And in al-Mujtaba, al-Baqqali said: If he listens to a woman crying to soften, there is no harm if he is safe from falling into fitnah, due to his (peace be upon him) listening to the women crying over Hamza. And fire is not followed in a brazier, nor a candle, and there is no harm in eulogizing the deceased, poetry or otherwise.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings: 1) One should stay with the funeral until after the prayer, as following is for that purpose. 2) Women are forbidden from attending funerals based on a clear hadith. 3) Wailing and screaming are disliked (makruh), but crying without noise is permissible. 4) If a hired wailer is present, the funeral may still be followed; the sunnah is not abandoned due to someone's innovation. 5) Listening to crying women is permissible if safe from fitnah, following the Prophet's example with Hamza. 6) Carrying fire or candles is prohibited. 7) Eulogizing the deceased, in poetry or prose, is permissible.

Key Terms
الاتباع (al-ittiba'): Following the funeral procession.
الجنازة (al-janazah): The funeral procession or the bier with the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main proof for the prohibition of women attending funerals?
A) A Quranic verse
B) A hadith where the Prophet said 'Return, you are sinful, not rewarded'
C) Consensus of scholars
D) Analogy to prayer

Key Takeaway
Women are forbidden from attending funerals based on an explicit prophetic command, and following the funeral is required until the prayer is completed.

Mourning Etiquette: Wailing, Crying, Eulogy, and Fire
Rulings on mourning practices: wailing, crying, fire, eulogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible crying and prohibited wailing, state the ruling on eulogy and carrying fire, and apply these rules in mourning scenarios.

Core Idea
Wailing is makruh tahrimi, crying without noise is permissible, eulogy is allowed, carrying fire is prohibited.

This passage continues with important rulings on how to mourn: the distinction between natural crying (permissible) and wailing (disliked), the permissibility of eulogy, and the prohibition of carrying fire. It also addresses how to handle the presence of a hired wailer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Acts and Their Rulings
The passage lists several acts: wailing (النوح), screaming (الصياح), crying (البكاء), listening to crying, carrying fire, and eulogizing. Each has a distinct ruling.
Wailing and screaming are 'يكره' (disliked), crying is 'لا بأس' (no harm), listening is permitted if safe, fire is prohibited, eulogy is permitted.
2
Understand the Reason for Wailing's Dislike
The text says wailing is disliked 'للنهي عنه' (due to prohibition). This indicates a clear prohibition, making it makruh tahrimi.
The proof is general, but Hanafi fiqh classifies it as prohibitively disliked.
3
Distinguish Between Crying and Wailing
Crying (البكاء) without loud noise is permissible, while wailing (النوح) with raised voice is disliked. The key difference is the manner.
The Prophet himself listened to women crying over Hamza, indicating permissibility.
4
Apply the Ruling on Following Despite a Wailer
If a hired wailer (نائحة) is present, the sunnah of following is not abandoned. The bid'ah of the wailer does not prevent following the sunnah.
This shows that one should not let the presence of innovation deter from performing sunnah.
5
Note the Prohibition of Fire and Permissibility of Eulogy
Carrying fire (in a brazier or candle) is not followed; it is prohibited. Eulogizing the deceased, whether in poetry or prose, is permissible.
Eulogy is allowed as long as it does not involve falsehood or wailing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He follows the funeral until he prays, because following was for the prayer upon her, so he should not return before achieving the purpose. Rulings on Condolence and Eulogizing
Detailed rulings on offering condolences and eulogizing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on condolence in Hanafi fiqh, identify disliked practices, and apply the recommended phrases and etiquette.

Core Idea
Condolence is sunnah; avoid jahiliyyah practices like sitting at doors or excessive praise.

Offering condolences (ta'ziyah) to the bereaved is a recommended act in Islam. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the rulings: it is sunnah, best on the first day, and certain practices are disliked (makruh). It also provides guidance on what to say and how to support the family. Understanding these rules helps you fulfill the sunnah properly and avoid innovations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling and evidence
Locate the statement that condolence is a sunnah and the hadith cited as proof. Understand that the hadith indicates reward, which in Hanafi usul makes the act sunnah.
The hadith is 'من عزى مصاباً فله مثل أجره'.
2
Note the best timing and venue
The text states that condolence is best on the first day. Sitting for condolence in a mosque for three days is disliked, but sitting elsewhere (e.g., at home) is permissible for three days.
Leaving it (not sitting) is better.
3
List the disliked (makruh) practices
Identify each makruh: sitting in mosque for three days, sitting at the doorstep, excessive praise of the deceased, repeating condolences, and condolence at the grave (some disliked).
These are based on jahiliyyah practices.
4
Learn the recommended supplication
The recommended phrase is: 'أعظم الله أجرك وأحسن عزاك وغفر لميتك'.
This is adab al-mu'azzi.
5
Understand the dispute on punishment by crying
The text presents a disagreement: some say the deceased is punished by family's crying, but the majority (عامة) hold the opposite view.
The Hanafi relied-upon view is that the deceased is not punished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتعزية للمصاب سنة للحديث «من عزى مصاباً فله مثل أجره» قال البقالي : ولا بأس بالجلوس للعزاء ثلاثة أيام في بيت أو مسجد وقد جلس رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لما قتل جعفر وزيد بن حارثة والناس يأتون ويعزونه والتعزية في اليوم الأول أفضل والجلوس في المسجد ثلاثة أيام للتعزية مكروه وفي غيره جاءت الرخصة ثلاثة أيام للرجال وتركه أحسن ويكره للمعزى أن يعزي ثانياً اهـ. كما وهي في التبيين أن يقول : أعظم الله أجرك وأحسن عزاك وغفر لميتك. ولا بأس بالجلوس إليها ثلاثاً من غير ارتكاب محظور من فرش البسط والأطعمة من أهل البيت لأنها تتخذ عند السرور ولا بأس بأن يتخذ لأهل الميت طعام اهـ. وفي الخانية : وإن اتخذ ولي الميت طعاماً للفقراء كان حسناً إذا كانوا بالغين، وإن كان في الورثة صغير لم يتخذ ذلك من التركة .اهـ. وفي الظهيرية : ويكره الجلوس على باب الدار للتعزية لأنه عمل أهل الجاهلية وقد نهي عنه وما يصنع في بلاد العجم من فرش البسط والقيام على قوارع الطرق من أقبح القبائح .اهـ. وفي التجنيس : ويكره الإفراط في مدح الميت عند جنازته لأن الجاهلية كانوا يذكرون في ذلك ما هو شبه المحال وفيه قال عليه الصلاة والسلام «من تعزى بعزاء الجاهلية فأعضوه بهن أبيه ولا تكنوا» اهـ . وفي القنية عن شداد: أكره التعزية عند القبر ذكره في المجرد اهـ وفي الظهيرية : وهل يعذب الميت ببكاء أهله عليه؟ فقال بعضهم : يعذب لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام إن الميت ليعذب ببكاء أهله» وقال عامة
And condolence for the afflicted is a sunnah due to the hadith: 'Whoever consoles the afflicted will have a reward like his.' Al-Baqqali said: There is no harm in sitting for condolence for three days in a house or mosque, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) sat when Ja'far and Zaid ibn Harithah were killed, and people came and offered condolences. Condolence on the first day is best, and sitting in the mosque for three days for condolence is disliked, and in other than it, license came for three days for men, and leaving it is better. And it is disliked for the one being consoled to offer condolences a second time. And it is in al-Tabyin to say: 'May Allah increase your reward, improve your consolation, and forgive your deceased.' And there is no harm in sitting for it for three days without committing a prohibition, such as laying out carpets and food from the household, because this is done at times of joy. And there is no harm in preparing food for the family of the deceased. And in al-Khaniyyah: If the guardian of the deceased prepares food for the poor, it is good if they are adults; and if there is a minor among the heirs, that is not taken from the estate. And in al-Zahiriyyah: Sitting at the door of the house for condolence is disliked because it is the practice of the People of Ignorance, and it has been prohibited. And what is done in the lands of the non-Arabs of laying out carpets and standing at crossroads is among the worst abominations. And in al-Tajnis: Excessive praise of the deceased at his funeral is disliked, because the People of Ignorance used to mention in that what is akin to impossible, and in it the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever consoles with the consolation of the Ignorance, then bite his father's penis and do not use a euphemism.' And in al-Qunyah from Shaddad: I dislike condolence at the grave, mentioned in al-Mujarrad. And in al-Zahiriyyah: Is the deceased punished by the crying of his family over him? Some say he is punished, due to the Prophet's saying: 'The deceased is indeed punished by the crying of his family over him.' And the majority...
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage gathers rulings on condolence (ta'ziyah). It is a sunnah, best on the first day. Sitting for condolence in a mosque for three days is disliked, but permissible elsewhere. The actual condolence should not be repeated. Specific phrases are recommended. Preparing food for the bereaved family is allowed, but not from the minor's estate. Sitting at the doorstep is makruh, as it resembles jahiliyyah. Excessive praise at the funeral is also makruh. There is a difference of opinion on whether the deceased is punished by family's crying; some say yes based on a hadith, but the majority hold a different view (the text cuts off).

Key Terms
التعزية (al-ta'ziyah): Offering condolences to the bereaved.
المعزى (al-mu'azzi): The person offering condolence.
المصاب (al-musab): The afflicted person (the one who lost a loved one).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is makruh in condolence?
A) Sitting in a house for three days
B) Sitting in a mosque for three days
C) Preparing food for the bereaved family
D) Saying the recommended prayer

Key Takeaway
Condolence is a sunnah; avoid jahiliyyah practices; the deceased is not punished by crying.

The Sunnah of Offering Condolence and Its Etiquettes
Rulings on offering condolence (ta'ziya) and its etiquettes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunna status of ta'ziya, distinguish between permissible and disliked practices regarding sitting and places, and apply these rulings to real scenarios.

Core Idea
Offering condolence is sunna; sitting for it in the mosque is makruh.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi ruling on condolence (ta'ziya). It establishes the sunna status based on a hadith and then details the best practices, permissible places, and disliked innovations. Understanding these nuances helps a Muslim fulfill this social duty correctly without falling into what is makruh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Basic Ruling and Its Proof
Read the opening sentence: 'Offering condolence to the afflicted is a sunna because of the hadith.' Recognize that the hadith promise of reward indicates desirability (sunna) in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is from Ibn Majah and Tirmidhi.
2
Determine the Best Time for Condolence
The text states condolence on the first day is best. Understand that while it is permissible later, delay beyond three days may be disliked as it renews grief.
3
Analyze the Ruling on Sitting for Condolence
Distinguish between sitting in a house (permissible with concession for three days) and sitting in a mosque (makruh). Note that even in a house, leaving the formal sitting is better.
The phrase 'sitting' refers to gathering to receive condolence.
4
Note the Prohibition of Repeating Condolence
The text explicitly says it is makruh for the bereaved to receive condolence a second time from the same person. This prevents prolonging grief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتعزية للمصاب سنة للحديث من عزى مصاباً فله مثل أجره»(۱) قال البقالي : ولا بأس بالجلوس للعزاء ثلاثة أيام في بيت أو مسجد وقد جلس رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لما قتل جعفر وزيد بن حارثة والناس يأتون ويعزونه والتعزية في اليوم الأول أفضل والجلوس في المسجد ثلاثة أيام للتعزية مكروه وفي غيره جاءت الرخصة ثلاثة أيام للرجال وتركه أحسن ويكره للمعزى أن يعزي ثانياً اهـ.
And offering condolence to the afflicted is a sunna because of the hadith: 'Whoever offers condolence to an afflicted person will have a reward like his.' Al-Baqqali said: There is no harm in sitting for condolence for three days in a house or mosque, and the Messenger of Allah ﷺ sat when Ja'far and Zayd ibn Haritha were killed, and people came and offered him condolence. Condolence on the first day is best. Sitting in the mosque for condolence for three days is makruh, but elsewhere the concession came for three days for men, though leaving it is better. It is makruh for the one being condoled to receive condolence a second time.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of offering condolence (ta'ziya) to the bereaved. It is a sunna, supported by a hadith promising reward equal to the afflicted person. The time for offering condolence is broad, but the best is on the first day after the death. However, it is better not to delay beyond three days because it may renew grief. The text mentions that sitting (making a gathering) for condolence for up to three days is permissible in a house or even in a mosque, but sitting in the mosque specifically for condolence is makruh because mosques are not meant for such gatherings. Elsewhere (like homes or community halls), the concession is given for men to sit for three days to receive visitors. However, even in those places, it is better (mustahabb) not to sit formally, to avoid resemblance to pre-Islamic practices or excessive mourning. It is also makruh for the bereaved person to receive condolence a second time from the same person, as it unnecessarily prolongs grief. The overall emphasis is on moderation: offering condolence is encouraged but without excess or innovation.

Key Terms
التعزية (al-ta'ziya): Offering condolence and comfort to the relatives of the deceased.
العزاء (al-'aza'): The gathering for condolence or the act of mourning; often used interchangeably with ta'ziya.

Does the Deceased Suffer from the Weeping of His Family?
Debate on whether the deceased is punished by the weeping of his family, with resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the deceased is not punished by family weeping and interpret the conflicting hadith in light of the Quranic principle of individual responsibility.

Core Idea
The deceased is not punished for others' weeping—individual responsibility is a Quranic principle that prevails over an apparent hadith.

This lesson tackles a classic issue where a hadith seems to contradict a clear Quranic verse. The Hanafi school, following the majority of scholars, resolves the conflict by interpreting the hadith in its historical context. Understanding this resolution trains the student in the hierarchy of evidence and the principle that definitive texts (Quran) supersede ambiguous or context-specific hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
The passage asks whether the deceased is punished (yu'adhdhab) by the weeping of his family. Some said yes, citing a hadith. The generality of scholars (including the Hanafi school) said no, citing Quran 6:164.
Note that the ruling here is about the state of the deceased, not an act of the living.
2
Examine the opposing proof (hadith)
The hadith 'The deceased is punished by the weeping of his family' appears in sound collections. It is the basis for the minority view.
The hadith is authentic but requires interpretation.
3
Examine the majority proof (Quran)
The verse 'And no bearer of burdens will bear the burden of another' (6:164) establishes the principle of individual responsibility. It is definitive (qat'i) in both transmission and meaning.
This verse is the primary dalil for the majority.
4
Understand the reconciliation (ta'wil)
The majority interpret the hadith as referring to the pre-Islamic practice where the deceased used to instruct his family to wail over him. Thus, the punishment is for his own command, not for the weeping itself. This removes the conflict with the Quran.
This is the key analytical step: using the Quran to contextualize and restrict the hadith.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the underlying principle
The Hanafi position is that the deceased is not punished by mere weeping. The underlying principle is that conflicting evidence is reconciled by giving priority to the stronger proof (Quran), and that apparent meanings of hadith may be qualified by other texts.
This demonstrates the Hanafi method of combining proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهل يعذب الميت ببكاء أهله عليه؟ فقال بعضهم : يعذب لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام إن الميت ليعذب ببكاء أهله»(۳) وقال عامة العلماء: لا يعذب لقوله تعالى ولا تزر وازرة وزر أخرى [الإنعام؛ ١٦٤] وتأويل الحديث أنهم في ذلك الزمان كانوا يوصون بالنوح عليهم فقال عليه الصلاة والسلام ذلك اهـ.
And is the deceased punished by the weeping of his family over him? Some said: He is punished because of his statement ﷺ: 'Verily the deceased is punished by the weeping of his family.' And the generality of scholars said: He is not punished because of His statement (Exalted): 'And no bearer of burdens will bear the burden of another' (Surah al-An'am 6:164). And the interpretation of the hadith is that in that time they used to bequeath wailing over them, so the Prophet ﷺ said that.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage addresses a controversial issue: whether the deceased suffers punishment due to the weeping and wailing of his surviving family members. The text presents two views. Some scholars hold that the deceased is indeed punished, citing the apparent meaning of a hadith: 'The deceased is punished by the weeping of his family.' However, the majority of scholars (عامة العلماء) reject this literal interpretation. They base their view on the clear Quranic verse from Surah al-An'am (6:164) which states that no soul bears the sin of another, establishing the principle of individual responsibility. They reconcile the hadith by explaining that it refers to the pre-Islamic practice where the deceased would actually instruct his family to wail over him (as a form of pride or custom). Since he commanded the wailing, he is held accountable for it, not for the weeping itself. Thus, the hadith does not mean that the deceased is punished for the mere crying of others without his involvement. This interpretation removes the apparent conflict with the Quran. The majority's view is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, as indicated by the author's conclusion with 'ذلك اهـ' (that is the end of the discussion).

Key Terms
بكاء الأهل (buka' al-ahl): The weeping of the family members over the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the majority view that the deceased is not punished by the weeping of his family?
A) A hadith stating the deceased is not punished.
B) The Quranic verse 'No bearer of burdens bears another's burden.'
C) Consensus of the companions.
D) The Prophet's own practice.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position affirms that the deceased is not punished by family weeping, interpreting the relevant hadith in a way that harmonizes with the Quranic principle of individual accountability.

Method of Carrying the Funeral Bier: The Sunna of Right-Side Precedence
Commentary explaining the sunna method of carrying the bier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunna method of carrying the bier with multiple carriers and explain why the order follows the principle of tayammun.

Core Idea
Carry the bier right side first to follow the Prophet's sunna of right-side precedence.

When many people carry the funeral bier, the Hanafi school recommends a specific order to maximize reward. This passage details the step-by-step method and its rationale, showing how the Prophet's practice of tayammun shapes every action.

Guided Path
1
State the legal status
Recognize that the method described is sunnah muakkadah (strongly recommended), not fard or wajib.
The ruling is based on a general hadith about tayammun, which indicates desirability, not obligation.
2
List the four placements in order
Write down the sequence: front right on right shoulder, back right on right shoulder, front left on left shoulder, back left on left shoulder.
The order ensures the carrier starts with their right and the deceased's right.
3
Identify the primary proof
The proof is the Prophet's love for starting with the right (tayammun). The commentator applies this principle to bier carrying.
The hadith 'كان النبي ﷺ يحب التيامن في كل شيء' is cited as the basis.
4
Explain the wisdom behind the order
The front is placed first because it is the beginning of the bier. Right parts come before left to honor the deceased's right side. The sequence allows the carrier to walk behind the bier, which is the preferred position.
If one were to start with the left front, they would have to walk in front, which is less virtuous.
5
Conclude the effect on validity
If the order is changed or omitted, the janaza remains valid, but the carrier loses the reward of following the sunna.
This is because the method is sunnah, not fard or wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وضع مقدمها على يمينه ثم مؤخرها ثم مقدمها على يسارك مؤخرها) بيان لإكمال السنة في حملها عند كثرة الحاملين إذا تناوبوا في حملها . وقوله ثم مؤخرها أي على يمينك . وقوله ثانياً ثم مؤخرها أي على يسارك . وهذا لأن النبي ﷺ كان يحب التيامن في كل شيء وإذا حمل هكذا حصلت البداءة بيمين الحامل ويمين الميت . وإنما بدأ بالأيمن المقدم دون المؤخر لأن المقدم أول الجنازة والبداءة بالشيء إنما يكون من أوله، ثم يضع مؤخرها الأيمن على يمينه لأنه لو وضع مقدمها الأيسر على يساره لاحتاج إلى المشي أمامها والمشي خلفها أفضل، ولأنه لو فعل ذلك أو وضع مؤخرها الأيسر على يساره تقدم الأيسر على الأيمن. وإنما يضع مقدمها الأيسر على يساره لأنه لو فعل هكذا يقع الفراغ خلف الجنازة فيمشي خلفها وهو أفضل لذلك كان كمال السنة كما وصفنا اهـ.
His statement (He places its front on his right, then its back, then its front on your left, then its back) is an explanation of completing the sunna in carrying it when there are many carriers taking turns. And his statement 'then its back' means on your right. And his statement secondly 'then its back' means on your left. This is because the Prophet ﷺ loved right-side precedence in everything. When carried like this, beginning is achieved with the carrier's right and the deceased's right. He began with the right front rather than the back because the front is the first part of the bier, and beginning with something is only from its start. Then he places its right back on his right because if he placed its left front on his left, he would need to walk in front of it, and walking behind it is better. Also, if he did that or placed its left back on his left, the left would precede the right. He places its left front on his left because if he does this, the empty part falls behind the bier, so he walks behind it, which is better. Therefore, the completion of the sunna is as described.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from the matn describing how to carry the funeral bier when multiple carriers take turns. The method is: 1) Place the right front corner of the bier on your right shoulder. 2) Then the right back corner on your right shoulder. 3) Then the left front on your left shoulder. 4) Then the left back on your left shoulder. The commentator explains that this order is based on the Prophet's love for starting with the right (tayammun) in all matters. By starting with the right front, the carrier begins with both his own right side and the deceased's right side. The front is placed first because it is the beginning of the bier. Then the right back follows on the same shoulder. The left parts are placed on the left shoulder. This arrangement ensures that the carrier walks behind the bier, which is the superior position. If one were to place the left front first, he would have to walk in front. The wisdom is that the carrier should be behind the bier, following it. Thus, this method achieves the ideal sunna.

Key Terms
التيامن (al-tayammun): Using the right side first or giving preference to the right in actions.
المقدم (al-muqaddam): The front part of the funeral bier (where the head of the deceased lies).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To make it easier for the carrier.
B) Because the Prophet loved right-side precedence and the front is the beginning of the bier.
C) So that the carrier walks in front of the bier.
D) Because the deceased's right side should be honored.

Key Takeaway
The sunna method of carrying the bier is a detailed practice based on the principle of tayammun, ensuring right-side precedence and the carrier walking behind.
