The Deceased Is Not Punished for Others' Wailing
Refutes punishment of deceased for wailing with Quran and hadith interpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the deceased is not punished for the wailing of his family, and how they reconcile the conflicting hadith.

Core Idea
The dead are not punished for others' sins; Quranic individual responsibility overrides.

The practice of wailing (niyahah) over the dead is prohibited in Islam, but a question arises: if the family of the deceased wails, does the deceased suffer punishment for their actions? Some early scholars held that punishment does occur, based on a certain hadith. The Hanafi school firmly refutes this, relying on a clear Qur'anic principle that no soul bears another's burden. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi argument and how they interpret the conflicting hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
Recognize that the question is whether the deceased is punished for the wailing of his family after his death. This is not about the ruling of wailing itself (which is haram), but about its effect on the deceased.
The issue is doctrinal, not a hukm taklifi.
2
State the Hanafi Position and Its Quranic Proof
The Hanafi school states that the deceased is not punished. The proof is the explicit Quranic verse (6:164): 'And no bearer of burdens will bear the burden of another.' This establishes individual accountability.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah, giving certainty.
3
Examine the Opposing Proof
The opposing view relies on a hadith that appears to indicate punishment for the deceased due to wailing. Identify that hadith and its apparent meaning.
The exact hadith is not quoted in this passage, but it is understood to be about punishment for wailing.
4
Understand the Hanafi Interpretation (Ta'wil)
The Hanafi scholars interpret the hadith by contextualizing it: the Prophet's statement applied to people who used to recommend wailing upon themselves. Thus the punishment is for the deceased's own recommendation, not for the act of others.
This ta'wil resolves the apparent conflict and preserves the Quranic principle.
5
Conclude with the Hanafi Tarjih
Because the Quranic text is clear and the hadith is interpreted in a manner consistent with it, the Hanafi position is definitive. The deceased is not punished for the wailing of others.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنائز فصل السلطان أحق بصلاته العلماء: لا يعذب لقوله تعالى ولا تزر وازرة وزر أخرى [الإنعام ؛ ١٦٤] وتأويل الحديث أنهم في ذلك الزمان كانوا يوصون بالنوح عليهم فقال عليه الصلاة والسلام ذلك اهـ.
The Book of Funerals. Chapter: The Sultan is more entitled to lead the prayer. The scholars: He (the dead) is not punished because of His statement, the Exalted, 'And no bearer of burdens will bear the burden of another' [Al-An'am 6:164]. And the interpretation of the hadith is that they in that time used to recommend wailing over them, so the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that (the hadith). End.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of whether the deceased is punished due to the wailing (niyahah) of his family. The author refutes the notion by citing Quran 6:164, which establishes individual responsibility. The apparent conflict with a hadith that seems to indicate punishment is resolved by interpreting the hadith as referring to a specific practice where the deceased himself recommended wailing, so the punishment is for his recommendation, not for the act of others. This is a standard Hanafi position.

Key Terms
النياحة (al-niyāḥah): Wailing over the dead, a pre-Islamic practice
تأويل (ta'wīl): Interpretation that reconciles a text with a stronger proof
ولا تزر وازرة وزر أخرى (wa lā taziru wāziratun wizra ukhra): And no bearer of burdens will bear the burden of another (Quran 6:164)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Because wailing was only practiced in pre-Islamic times

Key Takeaway
The clear Quranic principle that no soul bears the sin of another proves that the deceased is not punished for the wailing of his family; any seemingly contradictory hadith is interpreted in light of this principle.

Recommended Actions in Carrying and Walking with the Bier
Lists sunan: forty steps expiation, walking with head forward, placing bier transversely

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three recommended actions (sunan) in carrying and walking with the bier, explain the hadith on forty steps, and identify the linguistic variation of 'muqaddam'.

Core Idea
Carrying the bier for forty steps expiates forty major sins — a sunna, not an obligation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq presents three sunan related to funeral rites: the virtue of carrying the bier forty steps, walking with the head advanced, and placing the bier transversely before the qibla. The text also clarifies the correct pronunciation of muqaddam and mu’akhkhar. These acts are recommended (mandub) and not obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three recommended acts
List the three sunan: carrying forty steps, advancing the head (muqaddam), and transverse placement at the prayer place.
2
Locate the dalil for the first sunna
The hadith 'Whoever carries a funeral for forty steps, forty major sins are expiated' is cited.
This ahad hadith indicates recommendation.
3
Understand the fiqh status
These are sunna, not wajib. The hadith is ahad, so it indicates recommendation.
The Hanafi school classifies it as sunna, not fard.
4
Note the linguistic clarification
The word 'muqaddam' can be pronounced with kasr or fath of the dal; kasr is more eloquent. Similarly for 'mu'akhkhar'.
This is a minor lexical note.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينبغي أن يحمل من كل جانب عشر خطوات للحديث من حمل جنازة أربعين خطوة كفرت أربعين كبيرة كذا في البدائع. وذكر الأسبيحابي وفي حالة المشي بالجنازة يقدم الرأس، وإذا نزلوا به المصلى فإنه يوضع عرضاً للقبلة والمقدم بفتح الدال وكسرها والكسر أفصح كذا في الغاية. وكذا المؤخر. وفي ضياء الحلوم : المقدم بضم الميم وفتح الدال مشددة نقيض المؤخر، يقال ضرب مقدم وجهه وهو الناصية اهـ.
It is recommended to carry it from each side ten steps, due to the hadith: 'Whoever carries a funeral for forty steps, forty major sins are expiated' as in al-Bada'i'. And al-Isbijahbi mentioned: And when walking with the funeral, the head is advanced. And when they bring it to the prayer place, it is placed transversely facing the qibla. And (the word) al-muqaddam: with fath of the dal and kasr of the dal, and kasr is more eloquent as in al-Ghaya. Similarly al-mu'akhkhar. And in Diya' al-Hulum: al-muqaddam with damm of the mim and fathi of the dal with tashdid, opposite of al-mu'akhkhar. It is said: he struck the front of his face, i.e., the forehead.

Commentary
This passage presents additional sunan related to carrying the bier: the virtue of carrying it for forty steps to expiate major sins, the recommendation to walk with the head of the deceased advanced (i.e., the front of the bier forward), and the proper orientation of the bier at the prayer place (placed transversely facing the qibla). The text also includes linguistic notes on the pronunciation of 'muqaddam' and 'mu'akhkhar'.

Key Terms
المقدم (al-muqaddam): Front part of the bier or the head of the deceased
المؤخر (al-mu'akhkhar): Rear part of the bier
الجنازة (al-janazah): The funeral bier with the deceased

Checkpoint
What is the reward for carrying a funeral bier for forty steps according to the hadith?

B) Forty major sins are expiated

Key Takeaway
The three sunan of carrying the bier are: forty steps for expiation, advancing the head, and transverse placement at prayer — all are recommended, not obligatory.

Grave Construction: Niche, Trench, and Depth
Explains two grave types, proof, depth, and sea burial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methods of grave construction (lahd and shaqq), identify the preferred method based on soil condition, and explain the rulings on grave depth and burial at sea within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The niche (lahd) is the preferred sunnah; the trench (shaqq) is a valid alternative when the ground is soft.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi rulings on how to dig a grave. The source text from *al-Bahr al-Ra'iq* distinguishes two methods: the niche (lahd) and the trench (shaqq), each with specific conditions. The ruling is supported by a hadith and practical considerations about soil firmness. We also explore depth recommendations and the exceptional case of burial at sea.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Methods
Locate in the text the definitions of al-lahd (niche) and al-shaqq (trench). Note how each is constructed: the niche is a side cavity toward the qibla; the trench is a central ditch.
2
Analyze the Proof
The text cites the hadith 'اللحد لنا والشق لغيرنا'. Identify its source (Sunan of Abu Dawud) and explain how it indicates preference for the niche. Note that the hadith is ahad and zanni in transmission and meaning.
3
Apply the Soil Condition
The text states that the trench is recommended (istihsan) when the ground is soft, because the niche is difficult. Understand that the ruling is flexible: the niche is not always obligatory.
4
Examine Depth and Materials
The text mentions differing views on grave depth (half a man's height vs up to the chest) and says increasing is good. Also note the ruling on using a coffin when a niche is impossible, and the prohibition of throwing certain items into the grave.
5
Understand the Ship Burial Exception
The text gives the ruling for death on a ship: wash, shroud, pray, and throw the body into the sea. Recognize this as an exception when burial on land is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ( ويحفر القبر ويلحد) لحديث صاحب السنن مرفوعاً للحد لنا والشق لغيرنا يقال لحدت الميت وألحدت له لغتان واللحد بفتح اللام وضمها ـ كذا في الغاية وهو أن يحفر القبر بتمامه ثم يحفر في جانب القبلة منه حفيرة يوضع فيها الميت ويجعل ذلك كالبيت المسقف . والشق أن يحفر حفيرة في وسط القبر يوضع فيها الميت . واستحسنوا الشق فيما إذا كانت الأرض رخوة لتعذر اللحد، وإن تعذر اللحد فلا بأس بتابوت يتخذ للميت لكن السنة أن يفرش فيه التراب . كذا في غاية البيان. ولا فرق بين أن يكون التابوت كذا في التبيين. وذكر في الظهيرية معزياً إلى السرخسي في الجامع الصغير أنه من حجر أو حديد لا يجوز أن تطرح المضربة في القبر، وما روي عن عائشة فغير مشهور ولا يؤخذ به اهـ. واختلفوا في عمق القبر فقيل قدر نصف القامة، وقيل إلى الصدر وإن زادوا فحسن. وفي المحيط وغيره : ومن مات في السفينة يغسل ويكفن ويصلى عليه ويرمى في البحر .اهـ. وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يكن عن الأير بالهن تأديباً له وتنكيلاً ا.هـ.
His statement: (And he digs the grave and makes a niche) due to a hadith of the author of al-Sunan raised to the Prophet: 'The niche is for us, and the trench is for others.' It is said: 'lahadtu al-mayyita' and 'alhadtu lahu' are two dialects. Al-lahd (niche) with fath of lam and damm (of lam) – as in al-Ghaya – is that he digs the grave completely, then digs in its qibla side a small pit in which the deceased is placed, making it like a roofed room. And al-shaqq (trench) is that he digs a pit in the middle of the grave and places the deceased in it. They considered the trench recommended when the ground is soft due to difficulty of making a niche. And if a niche is not possible, there is no harm in a coffin made for the deceased, but the sunna is that soil is spread inside it. As in Ghayat al-Bayan. There is no difference whether the coffin is [made of stone or iron?] as in al-Tabyin. And it is mentioned in al-Zahiriyyah, citing al-Sarakhsi in al-Jami' al-Saghir, that it is not permissible to throw the mulching material in the grave, and what is narrated from Aisha is not well-known and not acted upon. End. They differed regarding the depth of the grave: some say half a man's height, some say up to the chest, and if they increase it is good. And in al-Muhit and others: whoever dies on a ship is washed, shrouded, prayed over, and thrown into the sea. End. It is conditioned upon [??].
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This lesson covers the rulings on grave construction. There are two methods: the niche (lahd) which is a cavity dug in the qibla side of the grave, and the trench (shaqq) which is a central ditch. The niche is preferred for firm soil; the trench is recommended when the ground is soft. If neither is possible, a coffin may be used, but it is sunna to spread soil inside. Depth is recommended to be up to the chest, though increasing is good. For burial at sea, the body is washed, shrouded, prayed over, and then thrown into the sea, with conditions noted.

Key Terms
اللحد (al-lahd): A niche excavated in the side of the grave toward the qibla to place the body
الشق (al-shaqq): A trench dug in the middle of the grave where the body is placed

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is the trench (shaqq) recommended over the niche (lahd)?
A) When the deceased was a non-Muslim
B) When the ground is soft and the niche is difficult
C) When there are many bodies to bury
D) When the grave is dug by a non-Muslim

Key Takeaway
The niche (lahd) is the sunnah method for grave construction in firm soil; the trench (shaqq) is recommended when the soil is soft, making the niche impractical.

Burial Procedures: Entering the Grave, Invocation, and Covering Materials
Details entering from qibla side, invocation, positioning body, and finishing grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on entering the grave from the qibla side, explain the dispute with the Shafi'i school, and identify the recommended materials for covering the grave.

Core Idea
The qibla side is most honored; entering from it is recommended, and baked bricks are disliked due to their association with fire.

Burial procedures involve several sunan acts that honor the deceased. This passage from al-Bahr al-Rai'iq details the Hanafi position on how to place the body in the grave, what to say, and how to finish the grave. It also addresses a dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding the method of insertion and the preference for unbaked bricks over baked ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute on entering the grave
Locate the contrasting methods: Hanafi enters from the qibla side, Shafi'i uses the 'sall' method (feet first from the side). Note the basis for each view.
The Hanafi view is based on honoring the qibla side as most honorable.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof and Shafi'i counter
The Hanafi position relies on conflicting narrations about the Prophet's burial and prefers the qibla side. The Shafi'i counter is based on a specific method. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in entry.
The text says 'رجحنا الأول' (we preferred the first).
3
Note other burial rulings
Review the invocation said when placing the body, the ruling on odd/even numbers entering the grave, who is entitled to enter for a woman, facing the deceased towards qibla, untying the knot, and the materials used to cover the grave.
Each of these is a separate sunnah with its own evidence.
4
Evaluate the reasoning on baked bricks
The text gives two reasons for disliking baked bricks: they are for sound building (grave is a place of tribulation) and they carry the effect of fire (bad omen). Note the critique by Imam Hamid al-Din that water heated by fire is still permissible, so the second reason might be weak.
The first reason remains, so stone and baked bricks are equal according to some.

القبلة بذلك أمر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ويكون على شقة الأيمن كما قدمناه. وفي الظهيرية : وإذا دفن الميت مستدبر القبلة وأهالوا التراب عليه فإنه لا ينبش ليجعل مستقبل القبلة، ولو بقي فيه متاع لإنسان على وزن كلمة ما يتخذ من الطين، والطن بضم الطاء الحزمة واختلف في المنسوج من القصب وما ينسج من البردي يكره في قولهم لأنه للتزيين. كذا في المجتبى قوله (لا) الآجر والخشب) لأنهما لأحكام البناء والقبر موضع البلاء ولأن بالآجر أثر النار فيكره تفاؤلاً كذا في الهداية. فعلى الأول يسوى بين الحجر والآجر، وعلى الثاني يفرق بينهما كذا في الغاية وأورد الإمام حميد الدين الضرير على التعليل الثاني أن الماء يسخن بالنار ومع ذلك يجوز استعماله فعلم أن أثر النار لا يضر.
His statement: (And he enters from the direction of the qibla) meaning the bier is placed on the qibla side of the grave and the deceased is carried from it and placed in the niche, so the one taking him faces the qibla when taking. And al-Shafi'i chose the method of 'al-sall' which is to place the bier on the right side of the qibla, place the legs of the deceased towards the grave lengthwise, then take the feet and insert them into the grave, moving until the feet reach their place and the head enters the grave. The narrations regarding the Prophet's entrance (into the grave) are conflicting, and we preferred the first because the qibla side is honorable, so entering from it is recommended. His statement: (And the one placing him says: 'Bismillah wa 'ala millati Rasulillah') as narrated in the hadith. And al-Sarakhsi said: i.e., 'Bismillah wada'nak wa 'ala millati Rasulillah sallamnak'. And in al-Zahiriyyah, he added: 'billahi wa fillah'. And in al-Bada'i', he added: 'wa fi sabilillah'. Then al-Maturidi said: This is not a supplication for the deceased because if he died upon the millah of the Messenger of Allah, his state cannot be changed; if he died upon other than that, he is not changed to the millah of the Messenger of Allah, but the believers are Allah's witnesses on earth, testifying to his death upon the millah. Upon this the sunna is based. It does not harm whether an odd or even number enters the grave. Al-Shafi'i chose odd number, considering the number of shrouds, washing, and perfuming. Our proof is that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) was buried, al-Abbas, al-Fadl ibn al-Abbas, Ali, and Suhayb entered (the grave). In al-Bada'i'. And a mahram relative is more entitled to enter the grave for a woman, likewise a non-mahram relative is more entitled than a stranger. If none, then strangers may place her, and women are not needed for placing. His statement: (And he faces him towards the qibla) with that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) commanded, and he is on his right side as we have mentioned previously. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If the deceased is buried facing away from the qibla and they heap soil over him, it is not to be exhumed to make him face the qibla. But if there remains property of a person in the grave, there is no harm in exhuming to remove the property. And it is narrated that al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba dropped his ring in the grave of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he kept insisting until the bricks were lifted and he took his ring and kissed between the eyes of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and then he used to boast of that and say: I am the one who tells you about the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). His statement: (And the knot is untied) because safety from spreading is achieved. His statement: (And he levels unbaked bricks and reeds over him) because on his grave the Prophet (peace be upon him) had placed unbaked bricks and a bundle of reeds. The word 'labin' is singular 'labinah' on the weight of 'kalimah', what is made from clay. 'Al-tinn' (with damm of the taa) means a bundle. And there is a difference of opinion regarding woven reeds and what is woven from papyrus: it is disliked in their view because it is for decoration. As in al-Mujtaba. His statement: (Not baked bricks and wood) because they are for sound building, and the grave is a place of tribulation, and because baked bricks have the effect of fire, so it is disliked as an omen, as in al-Hidayah. According to the first reasoning, stone and baked bricks are equal; according to the second, there is a distinction, as in al-Ghaya. Imam Hamid al-Din al-Darir objected to the second reasoning: water is heated by fire and still its use is permissible, so it is known that the effect of fire does not harm.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage covers multiple burial rulings: entering the grave from the qibla side (Hanafi position) versus from the feet (Shafi'i's 'sall' method), the invocation to be said when placing the body, the debate about odd/even numbers entering the grave, who is most entitled to enter the grave for a woman, the positioning of the body on its right side facing qibla, that a mistaken direction does not require exhumation, untying the knot of the shroud, and the materials used to cover the grave (unbaked bricks and reeds are sunna; baked bricks and wood are disliked due to association with fire and building strength). The text also includes a critique of the reasoning about fire by Imam Hamid al-Din.

Key Terms
السل (al-sall): Method of inserting the body into the grave feet-first from the side
اللحد (al-lahd): The niche in the side of the grave where the body is placed
اللبن (al-labin): Unbaked bricks made from clay

Entry into the Grave: Qibla Side vs. Al-Sall
Explanation of the recommended method for placing the deceased into the grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi method of placing the deceased into the grave from the qibla side and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument of al-sall.

Core Idea
The qibla side is venerated, so entry from it is recommended even though narrations conflict.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the proper method of placing the deceased into the grave during burial. The Hanafi school recommends that the bier be placed on the qibla side and the body taken from there into the niche (lahd), while Imam al-Shafi'i preferred a different method called al-sall (feet-first entry). The commentary resolves conflicting narrations by giving preponderance to the qibla side due to its honored status.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The bier is placed on the qibla side of the grave, and the deceased is carried from there into the lahḍ, with the carrier facing the qibla.
This is the recommended method.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Al-Shafi'i chose al-sall: the bier is placed to the right of the qibla, and the deceased is pulled in feet first.
Al-sall means 'drawing out'.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i relies on narrations about how the Prophet (peace be upon him) was placed into his grave.
The text notes that narrations are conflicting.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The narrations are conflicting, so the Hanafi school prefers the qibla side because that side is most honored.
The underlying principle: honoring the qibla takes precedence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is the orientation of the body during placement; both methods are valid, but the Hanafi method is considered mustahabb.
This affects the funeral practice but not the validity of the burial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ( ويدخل من قبل القبلة) وهو أن توضع الجنازة في جانب القبلة من القبر ويحمل الميت منه فيوضع في اللحد فيكون الآخذ له مستقبل القبلة حال الأخذ، واختار الشافعي السل وهو أن توضع الجنازة على يمين القبلة ويجعل رجلا الميت إلى القبر طولاً، ثم يؤخذ برجليه وتدخل رجلاه في القبر ويذهب به إلى أن تصير رجلاه إلى موضعهما ويدخل رأسه القبر، واضطربت الروايات في إدخاله عليه الصلاة والسلام ورجحنا الأول لأن جانب القبلة معظم فيستحب الإدخال منه .
His statement (and he enters from the direction of the qibla): That is, the bier is placed on the qibla side of the grave, and the deceased is carried from there and placed in the niche (lahd), so the one taking him faces the qibla at the time of taking. Al-Shafi'i chose al-sall (drawing out), which is: the bier is placed to the right of the qibla, and the two feet of the deceased are placed lengthwise toward the grave, then he is taken by his feet, his feet enter the grave, and he is taken until his feet reach their place, and his head enters the grave. The narrations about his (peace be upon him) entry are conflicting, and we prefer the first because the qibla side is venerated, so entry from it is recommended.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage discusses the proper method of placing the deceased into the grave. The Hanafi position is that the bier is placed on the qibla side of the grave, and the deceased is lifted from that side into the niche (lahd), with the person handling the body facing the qibla. Imam al-Shafi'i chose a different method called al-sall (literally 'drawing out'), where the bier is placed to the right of the qibla, the feet are positioned toward the grave, and the deceased is pulled in feet first. The author notes that the narrations regarding how the Prophet (peace be upon him) was placed into his grave are conflicting. The Hanafi school gives preponderance to the first method because the qibla side is honored and recommended for entry. This is an inter-madhhab dispute with practical consequences for funeral rites.

Key Terms
السل (al-sall): The method of drawing the deceased lengthwise into the grave from the foot end, as chosen by al-Shafi'i.
اللحد (al-lahd): A niche dug sideways in the grave to place the body.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) From the foot of the grave
B) From the qibla side
C) From the head of the grave
D) From the right side of the grave

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends entering the deceased from the qibla side because that side is venerated, even though narrations are conflicting.

The Sunnahs of Placing the Deceased and Facing Him to the Qibla
Explanation of sunnah phrases and facing qibla with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended phrases for placing the deceased, explain the ruling on facing the deceased to the qibla, and apply the Hanafi rule that exhumation is generally prohibited except to retrieve property.

Core Idea
Burial includes recommended phrases and a mandatory orientation to the Qibla; errors after burial do not require exhumation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains two important sunnahs of burial: the phrases the placer says when lowering the deceased, and the obligation to face the deceased towards the Qibla. It also clarifies a common misunderstanding that these phrases are a supplication for the deceased, and addresses a dispute with al-Shafi'i over whether an odd or even number of people should enter the grave. Finally, it discusses when exhumation is permitted—a question that arises in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah phrases
Find and memorize the recommended phrases as reported in hadith: 'Bismillah wa 'ala millati Rasulillah' and the expansions mentioned by later scholars. Understand that these are testimonies, not supplications.
Al-Maturidi emphasizes that the deceased's state is fixed; the believers merely bear witness.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof for the even/odd dispute
Al-Shafi'i prefers an odd number of people entering the grave, analogizing to the odd numbers of shrouds, washing, and fumigation. The Hanafi proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was buried by four men: al-Abbas, al-Fadl, Ali, and Suhayb. This shows that evenness is permissible.
The Hanafi position is that it does not harm whether the number is odd or even.
3
Understand the ruling on facing the deceased to the Qibla
The deceased must be placed on his right side facing the Qibla. This is based on a command of the Prophet (peace be upon him). If the deceased is buried incorrectly (e.g., with his back to the Qibla), he is not exhumed to correct the orientation.
Exception: exhumation is permitted to retrieve a valuable object, as illustrated by the story of al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah's ring.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ويقول واضعه باسم الله وعلى ملة رسول الله كذا ورد في الحديث. وقال السرخسي : أي بسم الله وضعناك وعلى ملة رسول الله سملناك وزاد في الظهيرية : بالله وفي الله . وزاد في البدائع : وفي سبيل الله . ثم قال الما تريدي وليس هذا بدعاء للميت لأنه إذا مات على ملة رسول الله لم يجز أن تبدل عليه الحالة وإن مات على غير ذلك لم يبدل إلى ملة رسول الله ولكن المؤمنين شهداء الله في الأرض يشهدون بوفاته على الملة. وعلى هذا جرت السنة. ولا يضر وتر دخل القبر أم شفع واختار الشافعي الوتر اعتباراً بعدد الكفن والغسل والإجمار. ولنا أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لما دفن أدخله العباس والفضل بن العباس وعلي كذا وصهيب . في البدائع . وذو الرحم المحرم أولى بإدخال المرأة القبر، وكذا الرحم غير المحرم أولى من الأجنبي، فإن لم يكن فلا بأس للأجانب وضعها ولا يحتاج إلى النساء للوضع قوله (ووجه إلى (القبلة بذلك أمر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ويكون على شقة الأيمن كما قدمناه. وفي الظهيرية : وإذا دفن الميت مستدبر القبلة وأهالوا التراب عليه فإنه لا ينبش ليجعل مستقبل القبلة، ولو بقي فيه متاع لإنسان فلا بأس بالنبش لإخراج المتاع، وروي أن المغيرة بن شعبة سقط خاتمه في قبر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فما زال بالصحابة حتى رفع اللبن وأخذ خاتمه وقبل بين عيني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم كان يفتخر بذلك ويقول : أنا أحدثكم برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم
His statement (and the one placing him says: In the name of Allah and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah). Thus it is reported in the hadith. Al-Sarakhsi said: Meaning, 'In the name of Allah we have placed you, and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah we have named you.' In al-Zahiriyyah it is added: 'With Allah and in Allah.' In al-Bada'i it is added: 'And in the path of Allah.' Then al-Maturidi said: This is not a supplication for the deceased, because if he died upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah, his state cannot be changed; if he died upon other than that, he is not changed to the religion of the Messenger of Allah. Rather, the believers are Allah's witnesses on earth, testifying to his death upon the religion. Upon this the sunnah proceeded. It does not harm whether the one entering the grave is odd or even; al-Shafi'i chose oddness considering the number of shrouds, washing, and fumigation. Our proof: when the Prophet (peace be upon him) was buried, he was entered by al-Abbas, al-Fadl ibn al-Abbas, Ali, and Suhayb, as in al-Bada'i. A mahram relative is more entitled to enter the woman into the grave; likewise a non-mahram relative is better than a stranger. If there is none, there is no harm for strangers to place her, and women are not needed for placement. His statement (and he faces him to the qibla): By this the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) commanded, and he is placed on his right side as we have mentioned. In al-Zahiriyyah: If the deceased is buried with his back to the qibla and they have thrown soil upon him, he is not dug up to be made facing the qibla. But if there remains a belonging of a person, there is no harm in digging to retrieve that belonging. It is narrated that al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah's ring fell into the grave of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he kept pressing the Companions until they removed the brick and he took his ring, and he kissed between the eyes of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). Then he used to boast of that and say: 'I am the one who tells you about the Messenger of Allah.'
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings. First, the recommended phrase when placing the deceased into the grave: 'Bismillah wa 'ala millati Rasulillah'. Scholars expanded on this, adding phrases like 'With Allah and in Allah' and 'In the path of Allah'. Al-Maturidi clarifies that this is not a supplication changing the deceased's state; rather, the believers testify that the person died on the religion of the Prophet. It is not necessary that the person entering the grave be an odd number, although al-Shafi'i prefers oddness by analogy to the odd numbers of shrouds, washing, and fumigation. The Hanafi proof is that the Prophet was entered by four men. Also, a mahram relative should enter a female deceased into the grave, then a non-mahram relative, then strangers. Women are not needed for placement. Second, the deceased must be placed on his right side facing the qibla. If he is buried facing away from the qibla, he is not exhumed to be reoriented, except to retrieve a valuable object, as in the story of al-Mughirah retrieving his ring from the Prophet's grave.

Key Terms
واضعه (wadi'uhu): The person who places the deceased into the grave (the one who lowers him into the lahd).
سملنا (sammalnaka): We have named you (i.e., we recite the name of the religion upon you).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if a deceased is buried with his back to the Qibla and soil has been thrown over him?
A) The grave must be dug up and the body reoriented.
B) The grave is left undisturbed; the burial is valid.
C) The grave is dug up only if the mistake is discovered within three days.
D) The grave is dug up only for a prophet or martyr.

Key Takeaway
Burial includes recommended phrases and a mandatory orientation to the Qibla; exhumation for correction is not allowed, but it is permitted to retrieve valuable items.

Ruling on Baked Bricks and Wood in the Grave
Ruling on grave materials with talil and objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using baked bricks and wood in the grave, explain the reasoning (ill omen of fire), and identify the exceptions where their use is permissible.

Core Idea
Baked bricks and wood are disliked in the grave due to the trace of fire as a bad omen, but permissible when necessary.

The Hanafi school prescribes sunnah materials for the grave: unbaked bricks (laban) and reeds, as practiced by the Prophet ﷺ. This lesson examines why baked bricks and wood are disliked (makruh tanzih), the objection raised by Imam Hamid al-Din al-Darir, and the nuanced positions of later scholars like Imam al-Sarakhsi. Understanding this ruling requires appreciating the role of ill omen (tafa'ul) in Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
The passage rules that baked bricks (ājurr) and wood are disliked (makruh tanzih) for use in the grave. The preferred materials are unbaked bricks and reeds.
The ruling is derived from practice of the Prophet ﷺ and reasoning about ill omen.
2
Examine the primary proof (dalil)
The dislike is based on two points: (1) baked bricks and wood are meant for strong building, while the grave is a place of trial; (2) baked bricks bear the trace of fire, which is disliked as a bad omen (tafa'ul).
The second point is the main focus of the passage.
3
Analyze the objection (i‘tirād)
Imam Hamid al-Din al-Darir objects: water heated by fire is permissible, so the trace of fire cannot be harmful. This is a qiyas (analogy) objection.
The objection challenges the consistency of the illa (effective cause).
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The response distinguishes: in baked brick the effect of fire is perceptible (mushāhadah), while in water it is not. Therefore, the illa differs.
This shows the importance of sensory perception in determining legal cause.
5
Note the exceptions (intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf)
Imam al-Sarakhsi restricts the prohibition to normal land; in moist/soft land, baked bricks and wood are permissible. Also, bricks above the grave (as protection from beasts) are allowed.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is dislike, but permissibility under necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وتحل العقدة لوقوع الأمن من الانتشار قوله (ويسوى اللبن عليه والقصب) لأنه جعل على قبره عليه الصلاة والسلام اللبن وطن من قصب واللبن واحده لبنة على وزن كلمة ما يتخذ من الطين، والطن بضم الطاء الحزمة واختلف في المنسوج من القصب وما ينسج من البردي يكره في قولهم لأنه للتزيين. كذا في المجتبى قوله (لا) الآجر والخشب) لأنهما لأحكام البناء والقبر موضع البلاء ولأن بالآجر أثر النار فيكره تفاؤلاً كذا في الهداية. فعلى الأول يسوى بين الحجر والآجر، وعلى الثاني يفرق بينهما كذا في الغاية وأورد الإمام حميد الدين الضرير على التعليل الثاني أن الماء يسخن بالنار ومع ذلك يجوز استعماله فعلم أن أثر النار لا يضر. وأجاب عنه في غاية البيان بالفرق لأن أثر النار في الآجر محسوس بالمشاهدة وفي الماء ليس بمشاهد أطلق المصنف في منعهما وقيده الإمام السرخسي بأن لا يكون الغالب على الأراضي النز والرخاوة فإن كان فلا بأس بهما كاتخاذ تابوت من حديد لهذا. وقيده في شرح المجمع بأن يكون حوله، وأما لو كان فوقه لا يكره لأنه يكون عصمة من السبع اهـ. وفي المغرب : الآجر الطين المطبوخ مقدمها الأيمن على يمينه أو بدونه ابتداء قوله : ( وأجاب عنه في غاية البيان الخ) أحسن من هذا ما في النهر وهو أن الآجر إنما كره في القبر تفاؤلاً لأن به أثر النار ألا ترى أنه يكره الإجمار عند القبر واتباع الجنازة بالنار بخلاف الغسل بالماء الحار لأنه يقع في البيت ولا يكره الإجمار فيه
His statement (and the knot is undone) because security from spreading is achieved. His statement (and leveling the brick upon it and the reeds) because upon the grave of the Prophet (peace be upon him) was placed brick and a bundle of reeds. The brick (laban) is one piece; its plural is libnah on the pattern of kalimah, made from clay. The bundle (tinn) with damm on the tā' is a bundle. There is disagreement about woven reeds and what is woven from papyrus; it is disliked according to their statement because it is for adornment. Thus in al-Mujtabā. His statement (not baked brick and wood) because they are for strong building and the grave is a place of trial, and because baked brick has the effect of fire, so it is disliked as an ill omen. Thus in al-Hidāyah. According to the first, stone and baked brick are equal; according to the second, they are distinguished. Thus in al-Ghāyah. Imam Hamid al-Din al-Darir objected to the second rationale that water is heated by fire and yet its use is permitted, so one knows that the effect of fire is not harmful. And he answered it in Ghāyat al-Bayān by the difference because the effect of fire in baked brick is perceptible by sight, while in water it is not perceptible. The author gave absolute prohibition, and Imam al-Sarakhsi restricted it: when the prevailing condition of the land is not moisture and softness; if it is so, then there is no harm in using them, such as making a coffin of iron for this. He restricted in Sharh al-Majma' that it be around him; as for above him, it is not disliked because it is a protection from wild beasts. In al-Mughrib: baked brick is cooked clay. His precedence: the right side on his right or without it. Beginning of his statement: (And he answered in Ghāyat al-Bayān etc.) Better than this is what is in al-Nahr, that baked brick is only disliked in the grave as an ill omen because it has the effect of fire; do you not see that fumigation at the grave and following the funeral procession with fire is disliked, unlike washing with hot water because it occurs in the house and fumigation is not disliked therein.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage discusses three points. First, the knot of the shroud is undone to prevent spreading. Second, the grave is leveled with unbaked bricks (laban) and reeds (qasab), as was done on the Prophet's grave. There is disagreement about woven reeds and papyrus; some scholars dislike them as ornamentation. Third, baked bricks (ājurr) and wood are disliked because they are for strong building and the grave is a place of trial, and baked bricks have the trace of fire, which is disliked as an ill omen. Imam Hamid al-Din al-Darir raised an objection: water can be heated by fire and is permissible, so fire's effect is not inherently harmful. The answer is that in baked brick the effect is visible, while in water it is not. The author initially prohibited both absolutely, but al-Sarakhsi restricted the prohibition to normal land; if the land is moist and soft, there is no harm, and even a metal coffin may be used. Another restriction: baked bricks around the grave are prohibited, but above it are allowed as protection from beasts. A later commentator in al-Nahr refines: the prohibition is because of ill omen, analogous to the dislike of fumigation at the grave and following with fire; hot water for washing is different because it is done in the house, not at the grave.

Key Terms
اللبن (al-laban): Unbaked brick made from clay, as used to level the grave.
التفاؤل (al-tafa'ul): Taking a bad omen; here the trace of fire in baked brick is considered a bad omen, so its use is disliked.
الآجر (al-ājurr): Baked brick; clay cooked in a kiln.
الإجمار (al-ijmār): Fumigation with fire; used as an analogy for the dislike of fire at the grave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Imam Hamid al-Din al-Darir object to the dislike of baked bricks?
A) He argued that baked bricks are stronger and thus safer
B) He argued that water heated by fire is permissible, so trace of fire is not harmful
C) He argued that the Prophet used baked bricks on his grave
D) He argued that the ill omen only applies to fire itself, not its trace

Key Takeaway
Baked bricks and wood are disliked in the grave due to the visible trace of fire as a bad omen, but this dislike is overcome by necessity (moist soil, protection), making their use permissible when needed.

Covering the Woman's Grave and Throwing Soil
Explanation of covering the grave of a woman, not a man, and the method of throwing soil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on covering a woman's grave and apply the method of throwing soil, including the intra-Hanafi dispute on sprinkling water.

Core Idea
Women's graves are covered for concealment; men's are not unless rain or snow.

The Hanafi school details specific practices for burial that reflect the principles of concealment for women and simplicity for men. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains two key actions: covering the grave of a woman during burial and the proper method of throwing soil. It also addresses a minor intra-madhhab difference regarding sprinkling water on the grave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main rulings
The passage first states that a woman's grave is covered (with a cloth or shelter) while a man's is not. Second, it explains that soil is thrown in a specific manner.
The ruling on covering is sunnah; throwing soil is recommended.
2
Understand the gender distinction
Women are covered because their state is built on concealment (sitr), while men are left exposed. However, if there is rain or snow, a man's grave may also be covered to protect the body.
The exception is based on necessity.
3
Analyze the dislike of extra soil
It is disliked (makruh) to add soil from outside the grave beyond what was dug out, because it resembles building up the grave, which is prohibited.
Only the excavated soil should be used.
4
Examine the dispute on sprinkling water
Sprinkling water on the grave is generally permissible as it helps level the soil. However, Abu Yusuf disliked it because it resembles plastering with clay (al-tatyin). The majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) permit it.
The mufta bihi is permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ويسجى قبرها لا قبره) لأن مبني حالهن على الستر والرجال على الكشف إلا أن يكون المطر أو ثلج. في المغرب: سجى الميت بثوب ستره قوله (ويهال (التراب ستراً له ويكره أن يزاد على التراب الذي أخرج من القبر لأن الزيادة عليه بمنزلة البناء، ويستحب أن يحثى عليه التراب. ولا بأس برش الماء على القبر لأنه تسوية له، وعن أبي يوسف كراهته لأنه يشبه التطيين
His statement (and her grave is covered, not his grave) because the principle of women is concealment and men is exposure, except if there is rain or snow. In al-Mughrib: He covered the deceased with a garment, i.e., he covered him. His statement (and soil is thrown) as a covering for him. It is disliked to add more soil than the soil that was taken out from the grave, because the addition is like building. It is recommended to throw handfuls of soil upon him. There is no harm in sprinkling water on the grave because it levels it, and from Abu Yusuf there is dislike of it because it resembles plastering with clay.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage explains two rulings. First, the grave of a woman is covered (with a cloth or shelter) during the burial process, while a man's grave is not covered, because women are generally to be concealed and men are exposed. However, if it is raining or snowing, a man's grave may also be covered. The term 'saja' means to cover with a garment. Second, regarding the throwing of soil: the soil that was excavated from the grave is thrown back; it is disliked to add extra soil from outside because that resembles building up the grave. It is recommended to throw handfuls of soil repeatedly. Sprinkling water on the grave is permissible as it helps level the soil, but according to Abu Yusuf, it is disliked because it resembles plastering with clay.

Key Terms
سجى (saja): To cover (the grave or the deceased) with a garment or cloth.
التطيين (al-tatyin): Plastering with clay; sprinkling water is disliked if it resembles this.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is obligatory
C) It is disliked
D) It is permissible

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school upholds concealment for women in burial, dislikes adding extra soil, and permits sprinkling water to level the grave (majority view).

Shaping the Grave and Prohibition of Plastering
Rulings with evidence and intra-madhhab differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the shape of the grave (tasnim) and the prohibition of plastering (tajsis), identify the hadith evidence, and apply the exceptions for need and custom.

Core Idea
The grave must be hump-shaped; plastering is forbidden by hadith but exceptions arise from necessity.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq discusses two key rulings concerning graves: the recommended shape (musannam) and the prohibition of plastering. You will learn the primary evidence from the Prophet's practice and hadith, as well as the intra-Hanafi differences on obligation and the exceptions that have arisen due to custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate the two distinct hukms: (1) the grave should be made musannam (hump-shaped) and not square; (2) plastering (tajsis) with gypsum is prohibited. Note the additional prohibitions of sitting, building, writing, and treading.
The text says 'ولا يجصص' (do not plaster) and provides the hadith of Jabir.
2
Examine the evidence for tasnim
The first ruling is based on the Prophet's practice (his grave was musannam) and his prohibition of squaring graves. The hadith of Ali about leveling raised graves is interpreted to apply only to excess beyond the sunnah shape.
The height is given as a handspan (shibr) or four fingers.
3
Analyze the evidence for the prohibition of plastering
The hadith of Jabir explicitly forbids plastering, sitting, building, writing, and treading. The word 'نهى' (forbade) indicates prohibition (haram) in Hanafi usul.
The prohibition is clear but can be overridden by istihsan (need).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi differences
On tasnim: some scholars (al-Zahiriyyah) say it is wajib, others (al-Mujtaba) say it is recommended. On plastering: the strict prohibition is relaxed for the box (sufṭ) due to custom, and writing is allowed if needed to preserve the grave's identity.
The later fatwa (fatawa mutakhkhirin) permits the box and writing in need.
5
Apply the exceptions
The custom of placing a wooden box over the grave is not considered plastering and is allowed. Writing the name of the deceased is permitted if it prevents loss of the grave or desecration.
The soil of the grave should not be removed unless the land was usurped.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ويسنم القبر ولا يربع) لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام نهى عن تربيع القبور ومن شاهد قبر النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام أخبر مسنم. في المغرب : قبر مسنم مرتفع غير مسطح ويسنم قدر شبر. وقيل: قدر أربع أصابع. وما ورد في الصحيح من حديث علي أن لا أدع قبراً مشرفاً إلا سويته»(۱) فمحمول على ما زاد على التسنيم. وصرح في الظهيرية بوجوب التسنيم، وفي المجتبى أنه باستحبابه . قوله (ولا يجصص) لحديث جابر : نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يجصص القبر، وأن يقعد عليه، وأن يبنى عليه وأن يكتب عليه، وأن يوطأ والتجصيص طلي البناء بالجص بالكسر والفتح كذا في المغرب. وفي الخلاصة : : ولا يجصص القبر ولا يطين ولا يرفع عليه بناء .. قالوا أراد به السفط الذي يجعل في ديارنا على القبر وقال في الفتاوى : اليوم اعتادوا السفط ولا بأس بالتطيين .اهـ. وفي الظهيرية : ولو وضع عليه شيء من الأشجار أو كتب عليه شيء فلا بأس به عند البعض .اهـ. والحديث المتقدم يمنع الكتابة فليكن المعول عليه لكن فصل في المحيط فقال : وإن احتيج إلى الكتابة حتى لا يذهب الأثر ولا يمتهن فلا بأس به،

ولا يخرج من القبر إلا أن تكون الأرض مغصوبة .
His statement (and the grave is made musannam and not made square) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade making graves square, and whoever saw the grave of the Prophet (peace be upon him) reported it was musannam. In al-Mughrib: A musannam grave is raised, not flat, and it is raised in height a handspan. It is also said: four fingers. What is recorded in the Sahih from the hadith of Ali, 'I do not leave any raised grave without leveling it,' is interpreted as referring to what exceeds the musannam shape. In al-Zahiriyyah it is stated that musannam is obligatory, while in al-Mujtabā it is recommended. His statement (and do not plaster) due to the hadith of Jabir: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade plastering the grave, sitting on it, building on it, writing on it, and treading on it. Plastering (tajsis) is coating the building with gypsum (jiss), with kasr or fath of the jīm, as in al-Mughrib. In al-Khulāṣah: Do not plaster the grave, nor plaster with clay, nor raise any building on it. They said: By this is meant the box (sufṭ) that is placed in our lands over the grave. In al-Fatāwā: Today they have become accustomed to the box, and there is no harm in plastering with clay. In al-Zahiriyyah: If something of trees is placed on it or something is written on it, there is no harm according to some. The aforementioned hadith prohibits writing, so let the reliance be upon it, but al-Muḥīṭ distinguished: If there is need for writing so that the trace is not lost and it is not desecrated, there is no harm. And no soil is taken out of the grave unless the land is usurped.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage covers the final rulings of shaping the grave. The grave should be made musannam (hump-shaped, raised in the middle), not square (murabba'), as the Prophet forbade squaring graves. The height of the hump is about a handspan or four fingers. The hadith of Ali about leveling raised graves applies to excess beyond the sunnah shape. There is a difference on whether musannam is obligatory (in al-Zahiriyyah) or recommended (in al-Mujtabā). Second, plastering (tajsis) the grave with gypsum is prohibited by the hadith of Jabir, along with sitting, building, writing, and treading on graves. Plastering includes coating with clay? The text clarifies that the prohibition of building includes the box (sufṭ) commonly placed over graves in some lands; today it has become customary and is allowed. Writing on graves is generally prohibited, but if needed to preserve the identity and prevent desecration, it is permitted according to al-Muḥīṭ. Lastly, the soil from the grave should not be removed except if the land is usurped, implying that the soil must be returned to the grave.

Key Terms
التسنيم (al-tasnim): Making the grave hump-shaped, raised in the middle like a camel's hump.
التجصيص (al-tajsis): Plastering with gypsum (jiss) or similar materials.
السفط (al-sufṭ): A wooden or metal box placed over the grave, common in some regions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the prohibition of plastering graves (tajsis) in the Hanafi school?
A) Quran verse on honoring the dead
B) Hadith of Jabir forbidding plastering
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy to building mosques

Key Takeaway
The grave should be made hump-shaped (musannam) and plastering with gypsum is prohibited, but customary boxes and writing for identification are allowed when needed.

Rulings on Graves: Tasnim, Tajsis, and Nabsh
Commentary on grave rulings from Kanz al-Daqa'iq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on making the grave humped (tasnim), plastering it (tajsis), and exhuming a body (nabsh), and identify the evidence and intra-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
The grave should be humped, not plastered, and exhumation is haram except for a human right.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on several key rulings related to graves. Based on prophetic practice and hadith, the Hanafi school distinguishes between the recommended shape of the grave and prohibited decorative acts. Understanding these rulings helps maintain proper reverence for the deceased while respecting the limits set by the Shari'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three main rulings
The passage discusses tasnim (humping the grave), tajsis (plastering), and nabsh (exhumation). For each, note the hukm level stated or implied.
Tasnim is recommended (mustahab) or obligatory (wajib) per some; tajsis is prohibited (makruh tahrimi); nabsh is haram except for a human right.
2
Locate the dalil for each ruling
Find the hadith or practice cited. For tajsis, the hadith of Jabir forbids plastering. For tasnim, the Prophet's grave was humped. For nabsh, the prohibition of exhumation is derived from hadith and consensus.
The hadith: 'نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يجصص القبر...'
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on tasnim
The passage mentions two positions: al-Zahiriyya says wajib, al-Mujtaba says mustahab. Identify the reason for difference and the mufta bihi.
Mufta bihi is istihbab (recommendation) as preferred by al-Nahr.
4
Understand exceptions for nabsh
Exhumation is normally haram, but permitted for a human right (haqq adami), e.g., stolen property, usurped land, or a stolen shroud. Identify the conditions.
The passage cites the case of Abu Righal for a golden staff.
5
Apply the principles to modern scenarios
Consider how these rulings apply today: plastering with cement, building structures, moving bodies for emotional reasons. Refer to the qualifications by later scholars.
The allowance of a 'safat' (basket) shows custom can modify strict prohibition.

The book of funerals. Section: The ruler has more right to his prayer. Soil and the grave is made humped and not squared, nor plastered, nor is the body taken out of the grave unless the land is usurped. And he answered in Ghayat al-Bayan with a distinction because the effect of fire in bricks is perceived by sight, while in water it is not perceived. The author made it absolute in prohibiting both, but Imam al-Sarakhsi qualified it: if the majority of lands are not marshy and soft, then there is no harm in them, like making a coffin of iron for this. And he qualified it in Sharh al-Majma' that it is around him; as for above him, it is not disliked because it is a protection from beasts. In al-Maghrib: bricks are baked clay. His statement: and her grave is covered, not his grave, because the condition of women is concealment, and men are uncovered unless there is rain or snow. In al-Maghrib: the dead is covered with a garment. His statement: and soil is poured as a covering, and it is disliked to add more soil than what was taken out of the grave because the addition is like building, and it is recommended to pour soil on it. There is no harm in sprinkling water on the grave because it levels it, and from Abu Yusuf is its disapproval because it resembles plastering. His statement: and the grave is made humped and not squared, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade squaring graves, and whoever saw the Prophet's grave reported it was humped. In al-Maghrib: a humped grave is elevated, not flat, and it is humped about a handspan, and some say four fingers. And what is reported in Sahih from Ali: 'I will not leave an elevated grave without leveling it' is understood as what exceeds the hump. And in al-Zahiriyya it is stated that humping is obligatory, while in al-Mujtaba it is recommended. His statement: and not plastered, due to the hadith of Jabir: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade plastering the grave, sitting on it, building over it, writing on it, and treading on it. Plastering is coating the building with gypsum. In al-Khulasa: the grave should not be plastered, nor mudded, nor built upon... They said what is meant is the basket that is placed in our lands on the grave, and in al-Fatawa: nowadays they have become accustomed to the basket and there is no harm in mudding. In al-Zahiriyya: if something of trees is placed on it or something written on it, there is no harm according to some. The above hadith forbids writing, so reliance should be on that, but al-Muhit distinguished: if writing is needed so that the trace is not lost and it is not dishonored, there is no harm. His statement: (and he answered in Ghayat al-Bayan etc.) Better than this is what is in al-Nahr: that bricks are only disliked in the grave as an omen because they have the effect of fire; do you not see that perfuming with fire is disliked at the grave and following the funeral with fire, unlike washing with hot water because it is in the house and perfuming with fire there is not disliked? And to this the commentator referred. The author's statement: and her grave is covered. al-Ramli said: it is obligatory, as stated by al-Yalai. So writing without an excuse is not allowed. In al-Mujtaba: it is disliked to tread on the grave, sit on it, sleep on it, relieve oneself of urine or stool on it, pray on it or towards it. Then walking on it is disliked, but on the coffin it is permitted according to some, like walking on a roof. In al-Khulasa: if one finds a path in the cemetery and thinks it is a newly made path, he should not walk there; if it is not in his mind, there is no harm in walking in it. In Fath al-Qadir: sitting on the grave and treading on it is disliked at that time. What people do of burying their relatives and then burying others around them, and a lot of treading on those graves until one reaches his relative's grave is disliked. In al-Muhit and others: two or three should not be buried in one grave except in necessity; the man is placed facing the qibla, then behind him the boy, then behind him the hermaphrodite, then behind him the woman, and between every two dead a barrier of soil is placed so that they become like two graves. Thus the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered for the martyrs of Uhud and said: 'Present those who memorized more Quran.' In Fath al-Qadir: burial in places called fasaqi is disliked. This is due to several reasons: first, lack of niche; second, burying a group in one grave without necessity; third, mixing of men and women without a barrier as is common in many of them; fourth, plastering and building on them. In al-Bada'i: Abu Hanifa said: one should not pray over a dead person among the graves; Ali and Ibn Abbas disliked that; if they prayed, it suffices them. His statement: nor is the body taken out of the grave unless the land is usurped, i.e., after soil has been poured over it, it is not permissible to take it out without necessity due to the prohibition of exhumation, and they stated its unlawfulness. His indication that the land is usurped is to permit exhumation for the right of a human, such as if his property falls into it, or he is shrouded in a stolen garment, or buried in the property of another, or buried with money to revive the right of the needy. The Prophet permitted exhumation of the grave of Abu Righal for a golden staff with him. As in al-Mujtaba. They said: even if the money is a dirham. And this includes when the pre-emptor takes it, for he may also exhume for his right as in Fath al-Qadir. And al-Tabyin mentioned that the owner of the land has the choice: if he wishes, he takes it out, or if he wishes, he levels it with the land and benefits from it for agriculture or other purposes. The author's statement indicates that if placed other than facing the qibla, or on the left side, or his head where his feet should be, or buried without washing and soil poured over him, then he should not be exhumed. Al-Bada'i said: because exhumation is unlawful as a right of Allah. In Fath al-Qadir: the consensus of the scholars regarding a woman whose son was buried while she was absent in another country and she could not bear it and wanted to move him: she is not allowed that; the permissibility of some later anomalies is not relied upon. The author made it absolute, including whether the time is long or short as in al-Fatawa. The author did not speak about moving the dead from one place to another before burial. In al-Waqi'at and al-Tajnis: the slain... Book of the Hermaphrodite. His statement: (recommended, in al-Nahr: it is more appropriate. His statement: (which are called fasaqi) is like a room built with construction that accommodates a group standing etc. As in al-Imdad. His statement: (they) meaning the dislike.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering multiple rulings related to graves and burial. The author first discusses the soil and shape of the grave: the grave should be made humped (musannam) and not squared, plastering is prohibited, and the body should not be exhumed except in cases of usurped land. He then addresses various issues: using bricks in the grave is disliked if the ground is marshy, covering the grave of a woman is obligatory due to modesty, sprinkling water is permissible, and adding extra soil is disliked. The main evidence for tasnim (humping) is the prophetic practice and the hadith forbidding squaring. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether tasnim is obligatory or recommended: al-Zahiriyya says obligatory, al-Mujtaba says recommended. Plastering is prohibited based on Jabir's hadith, but later scholars allowed a 'safat' (basket) due to custom. Writing on graves is generally prohibited unless necessary. The passage then discusses exhumation: it is haram except for a human right, such as reclaiming stolen property or burying in usurped land. Exhumation for moving the body due to emotional reasons is not allowed. The text also covers disliked acts: treading on graves, sitting, building, and burial in 'fasaqi' (built structures) due to lack of niche, mixing genders, etc. This passage provides a comprehensive view of Hanafi grave etiquette with proofs from hadith and scholarly consensus.

Key Terms
تسنيم (tasnīm): Making the grave raised like a camel's hump, not flat.
تجصيص (tajṣīṣ): Plastering the grave with gypsum or lime.
نبش (nabsh): Exhuming a buried body by digging up the grave.
سفط (safat): A basket or covering placed over a grave, allowed by custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on plastering a grave (tajsis) according to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage?
A) It is recommended (mustahab) because it beautifies the grave.
B) It is permissible (mubah) with no dislike.
C) It is prohibited (makruh tahrimi) based on the hadith of Jabir.
D) It is obligatory (wajib) for protection from animals.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school maintains that graves should be humped, not plastered, and exhumation is only permitted for a valid human right, not emotional reasons.

Grave Etiquette: Disliked Actions, Multiple Burials, and Fasaqi
Collection of rulings on grave etiquette

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on grave etiquette including actions that are disliked (makruh), explain the conditions for multiple burials, and identify the reasons why burial in fasaqi is disliked.

Core Idea
Respecting the dead: stepping, sitting, praying on or towards a grave is disliked; multiple burials only when necessary with proper order.

This passage compiles rulings from multiple Hanafi sources on proper conduct towards graves. It covers actions that are disliked, the rules for multiple burials, and the prohibition of certain burial structures. The Hanafi school emphasizes maintaining the sanctity of graves and avoiding innovations.

Guided Path
1
Identify disliked actions on graves
List the actions explicitly stated as makruh in the passage: stepping, sitting, sleeping, relieving oneself, praying upon or towards the grave.
These are from al-Mujtaba.
2
Distinguish walking on grave vs. coffin
Note that walking directly on the grave is disliked, but walking on a coffin is permissible according to some scholars, analogous to walking on a roof.
This distinction is important for practical situations.
3
Understand multiple burial rulings
Burying two or three in one grave is only allowed when necessary. The order: man, boy, khuntha, woman, with a dirt barrier between each.
This follows the Prophet's command at Uhud.
4
Explain why fasaqi are disliked
List the four reasons: lack of lahd, group burial without necessity, mixing genders without barrier, and plastering/building.
From Fath al-Qadir and al-Bada'i.
5
Note the ruling on praying between graves
Abu Hanifa considered it inappropriate but valid if done; Ali and Ibn Abbas disliked it.
Even if disliked, the prayer is sufficient.

فأما الكتابة من غير عذر فلا .اهـ. وفي المجتبى : ويكره أن يطأ القبر أو يجلس أو ينام عليه أو يقضى عليه حاجة من بول أو غائط أو يصلى عليه أو إليه ثم المشي عليه يكره وعلى التابوت يجوز عند بعضهم كالمشي على السقف اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : ولو وجد طريقاً في المقبرة وهو يظن أنه طريق أحدثوه لا يمشي في ذلك وإن لم يقع ذلك في ضميره لا بأس بأن يمشي فيه اهـ. وفي فتح القدير : ويكره الجلوس على القبر ووطؤه حينئذ فما تصنعه الناس من دفنت أقاربه ثم دفنت حواليهم خلق من وطء تلك القبور إلى أن يصل إلى قبر قريبه مكروه اهـ. وفي المحيط وغيره ولا يدفن اثنان وثلاثة في قبر واحد إلا عند الحاجة يوضع الرجل مما يلي القبلة ثم خلفه الغلام ثم خلفه الخنثى ثم خلفه المرأة، ويجعل بين كل ميتين حاجزاً من التراب ليصير في حكم قبرين هكذا أمر النبي الله في شهداء أحد وقال : قدموا أكثرهم قرآناً اهـ. وفي فتح القدير : ويكره الدفن في الأماكن التي تسمى فساقي .اهـ. وهي من وجوه: الأول عدم اللحد. الثاني دفن الجماعة في قبر واحد لغير ضرورة الثالث اختلاط الرجال بالنساء من غير حاجز كما هو الواقع في كثير منها . الرابع تجصيصها والبناء عليها. وفي البدائع قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله : ولا ينبغي أن يصلى على ميت بين القبور وكان علي وابن عباس يكرهان ذلك فإن صلوا أجزأهم اهـ. قوله : (باستحبابه قال في النهر : وهو أولى قوله : (التي تسمى فساقي) هي كبيت معقود بالبناء يسع جماعة قياماً ونحوه . كذا في الإمداد قوله : (وهي) أي الكراهة.
As for writing without excuse, it is not [allowed]. In al-Mujtaba: It is disliked to step on a grave, sit, sleep, relieve oneself of urine or stool, pray upon or towards it. Walking on it is disliked, but on a coffin it is permitted according to some, like walking on a roof. In al-Khulasa: If one finds a path in the cemetery and thinks it is a path they made, he should not walk in it; if he does not have that impression, there is no harm in walking in it. In Fath al-Qadir: Sitting and stepping on the grave is disliked. What people do when they bury their relatives and then bury around them, stepping on those graves to reach their relative's grave, is disliked. In al-Muhit and others: Two or three should not be buried in one grave except when necessary. The man is placed next to the qibla, then the boy behind him, then the khuntha, then the woman behind him. A barrier of earth is placed between each two deceased to make it like two graves. Thus the Prophet ﷺ commanded for the martyrs of Uhud and said: 'Put forward those who have more Qur'an.' In Fath al-Qadir: It is disliked to bury in places called 'Fasaqi'. These are from aspects: first, lack of lahd; second, burying a group in one grave without necessity; third, mixing of men and women without a barrier as occurs in many of them; fourth, plastering and building upon them. In al-Bada'i: Abu Hanifa said: It is not appropriate to pray over a deceased between graves, and 'Ali and Ibn 'Abbas disliked that. If they pray, it suffices them. His saying: (concerning its recommendation) said in al-Nahr: It is better. His saying: (places called Fasaqi) it is like a house built with structure that accommodates a standing group and similar. Thus in al-Imdad. His saying: (And it) refers to the disliked.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage collects rulings from various Hanafi works on proper conduct regarding graves. It begins by stating that writing [on graves?] is not allowed without excuse. Then from al-Mujtaba, it lists actions that are disliked (makruh) on graves: stepping, sitting, sleeping, relieving oneself, and praying upon or towards the grave. Walking directly on the grave is disliked, but walking on a coffin placed on the grave is permitted by some scholars, analogized to walking on a roof. From al-Khulasa: if a path in the cemetery is newly made, one should avoid walking on it if he suspects it was made by the cemetery owners. From Fath al-Qadir: sitting and stepping on graves is disliked, and the common practice of walking over other graves to reach a relative's grave is also disliked. From al-Muhit: burying two or three in one grave is only allowed when necessary. The order: man closest to qibla, then boy, then khuntha, then woman. A dirt barrier between each resembles two separate graves. This was the Prophet's practice at Uhud. From Fath al-Qadir: burial in 'fasaqi'—enclosed structures—is disliked for four reasons: no lahd (niche), group burial without need, gender mixing without barrier, and plastering/building. From al-Bada'i: Abu Hanifa said it is not appropriate to pray over a dead person between graves, though if done, it suffices. The commentary then explains the term 'fasaqi' as a built structure for standing.

Key Terms
اللحد (al-lahd): A niche on the side of the grave facing the qibla where the deceased is placed.
فساقي (fasāqī): Built structures in cemeteries where multiple deceased are placed without proper lahds.
الخنثى (al-khunthā): A hermaphrodite; in burial order, placed after a boy and before a woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Prohibited (haram)
D) Recommended (mustahabb)

Key Takeaway
The sanctity of graves requires avoiding all actions that can be seen as disrespectful, and multiple burials are only permitted under strict conditions with proper order and barriers.

Ruling on Exhumation of Graves (Nabsh)
Clarifying when it is permissible to exhume a body from a grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general ruling on exhumation in the Hanafi school, identify the exception for huquq al-ibad, and apply the principle to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Exhumation is haram unless a human right (haqq adami) is at stake.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the ruling on removing a body from a grave. The general rule is prohibition, but specific exceptions arise when human rights are involved. Understanding the distinction between huquq Allah and huquq al-ibad is key to applying this ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
The passage begins by affirming that after burial, exhumation is not permitted without necessity and scholars have declared it haram.
2
Recognize the exception basis
The exception is for a human right (haqq adami), such as property rights. Emotional reasons do not qualify.
3
List the examples provided
The text gives concrete examples: usurped land, stolen shroud, property buried with deceased, and pre-emption right.
4
Understand the rationale
Exhumation is a right of Allah (haqq Allah) and cannot be violated except when a human right takes precedence because huquq al-ibad may override huquq Allah in certain cases.
5
Apply the rule to borderline cases
Incorrect burial direction or missing ghusl do not justify exhumation because those are huquq Allah. Emotional desires are also insufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ولا يخرج من القبر إلا أن تكون الأرض مغصوبة أي بعدما أهيل التراب عليه لا يجوز إخراجه لغير ضرورة للنهي الوارد عن نبشه وصرحوا بحرمته. وأشار بكون الأرض مغصوبة إلى أن يجوز نبشه لحق الآدمي كما إذا سقط فيها متاعه أو كفن بثوب مغصوب أو دفن في ملك الغير أو دفن معه مال إحياء لحق المحتاج قد أباح النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نبش قبر أبي رعال لعصا من ذهب معه. كذا في المجتبى. قالوا؛ ولو كان المال درهماً. ودخل فيه ما إذا أخذها الشفيع فإنه ينبش أيضاً لحقه كما في فتح القدير. وذكر في التبيين أن صاحب الأرض مخير إن شاء أخرجه منها وإن شاء ساواه مع الأرض وانتفع بها زراعة أو غيرها. وأفاد كلام المصنف أنه لو وضع لغير القبلة أو على شقة الأيسر أو جعل رأسه في موضع رجليه أو دفن بلا غسل وأهيل عليه التراب فإنه لا ينبش. قال في البدائع : لأن النبش حرام حقاً لله تعالى. وفي فتح القدير : واتفقت كلمة المشايخ في امرأة دفن ابنها وهي غائبة في غير بلدها فلم تصبر وأرادت نقله أنه لا يسعها ذلك، فتجويز شواذ بعض المتأخرين لا يلتفت إليه اهـ. وأطلق المصنف فشمل ما إذا بعدت المدة أو قصرت كما في الفتاوى.
His saying: 'He should not be removed from the grave unless the land is usurped' meaning after earth has been cast upon him, it is not permissible to remove him without necessity due to the prohibition of exhumation, and they explicitly stated its prohibition. He indicated that if the land is usurped, exhumation is permitted for the right of a human, such as if his property falls into it, or he was shrouded in a stolen garment, or buried in someone else's property, or property was buried with him to revive the right of the needy. The Prophet ﷺ permitted exhumation of Abu Ri'al's grave for a golden stick with him. Thus in al-Mujtaba. They said: even if the property is a dirham. Included is if the preemptor (shafi') takes it, he may also exhume for his right as in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Tabyin: The owner of the land has the choice: if he wishes he may remove it, or if he wishes he may level it with the land and use it for cultivation or otherwise. The author's statement conveys that if the deceased was placed not facing the qibla, or on his left side, or his head placed where his feet should be, or buried without washing and earth was cast, he is not exhumed. In al-Bada'i: Because exhumation is prohibited as a right of Allah. In Fath al-Qadir: The consensus of the scholars regarding a woman whose son was buried while she was absent in another land, and she could not bear it and wanted to move him, is that it is not permissible for her. The permission of some anomalous later scholars is not regarded. The author's absolute statement includes whether the period is long or short, as in al-Fatawa.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement 'He should not be removed from the grave unless the land is usurped.' It begins by affirming the general rule: after burial, exhumation is not permitted without necessity, and scholars have declared it haram. The exception is when there is a human right (haqq adami) involved. Examples include: if the deceased's property falls into the grave, if he was shrouded in a stolen cloth, if the land itself is usurped, or if money was buried with him. These involve rights of others, so exhumation is allowed, even for as little as a dirham. The author cites the hadith of the Prophet permitting exhumation of Abu Ri'al's grave for a golden stick. The right of pre-emption (shuf'a) also allows exhumation. The landowner whose land is usurped may either remove the body or level the grave and use the land. However, if the deceased was placed incorrectly (not facing qibla, etc.) or buried without ghusl, exhumation is still not allowed because these are rights of Allah (huquq Allah). The consensus of the scholars is that emotional reasons do not justify exhumation; moving a body for emotional reasons is not permitted. The ruling applies regardless of how much time has passed.

Key Terms
نبش (nabsh): Exhumation, the act of digging up a grave to remove the deceased.
حق الآدمي (haqq al-ādami): A right belonging to a human being, such as property rights, as opposed to the rights of Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, in which case is exhumation of a grave permitted?
A) If the deceased was not facing the qibla
B) If the land is usurped and the owner wants to reclaim it
C) If the deceased was buried without ghusl
D) If the family feels emotional distress

Key Takeaway
Exhumation is generally prohibited as a right of Allah, but permitted if a human right (e.g., property) is at stake.

Transferring a Dead Body: Ruling and Proofs
Expansion on the ruling of transferring a body

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on transferring a deceased person from one city to another before burial, identify the supporting proofs, and explain the reasoning behind the karaha.

Core Idea
Transferring a body to another city is disliked; short distances are permissible.

The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq did not address the issue of transferring a body. The commentaries expand on it, citing reports from Aisha and actions of earlier prophets. The Hanafi school concludes that long-distance transfer is makruh due to delay and lack of benefit, while short transfers are allowed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is transferring a deceased person from one place to another before burial. The ruling is makruh (disliked) for long distances, permissible for short distances.
2
Locate the primary proofs
The main proof is the report of Aisha expressing disapproval of transferring her brother from Syria. Additional examples include the transport of prophets Ya'qub and Yusuf, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas.
These are historical reports, not necessarily binding as legal evidence.
3
Evaluate the strength of the prophetic proofs
The actions of previous prophets (shar' man qablana) are not binding unless confirmed by Islamic sources. The later scholars relied on the reasoning of delay in burial.
Al-Maqdisi and others note that the condition for it being a law for us is not met.
4
Understand the tarjih
Al-Tajiyyah and al-Tajnīs firmly state that transfer to another city is makruh. This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position, despite some later scholars permitting it.

Source Text
